Local News

New Regulations for Telephone in Concessions Implemented from Midnight Tonight Metering Charges for Numbers Exceeding Allotment Post Office Does Not Accept Proposal to Organize Communication Vehicles City Federation Continues to Support Telephone Issue Committee 106

The new regulations of the Shanghai Telephone Company in the concessions, despite repeated objections from various sectors, have ultimately been implemented effectively. A reporter from the New Sound News Agency inquired with the company yesterday morning and learned that the new regulations, after being approved by the Public Concession’s工部局and the French Concession’s公董局, will equip all 48,671 subscribers’ lines with a meter. This project has already been completed and will be activated after twelve o'clock last night. Any telephone that dials five consecutive numbers and receives a response from the other party will be charged once by the meter. However, due to difficulties in dialing, "01," calls to major venues, city centers, Jiangwan, Wusong, Nanshi, Zhabei, Nanxiang, Zhenru, Pudong, Longhua, Baoshan “02”, and long-distance calls “03”, inquiries “09”, will generally not be counted. City area calls and long-distance calls will still be handled according to previous regulations. Monthly fees are paid in advance, and overage fees are settled in the following month. Business telephones pay ten yuan and can make 150 metered calls. Residential telephones pay six yuan and fifty cents and can make 100 metered calls. Overage fees are three cents per metered call. The Special District Telephone Issue Committee, due to ineffective negotiations, has scheduled a joint meeting of various groups on the afternoon of March 10 to prepare for dissolution.

Statement from Taxpayers' Association A spokesperson for the Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association stated to reporters yesterday that the association has never expressed "approval or acceptance" of the Shanghai Telephone Company's new price list. This should be solemnly declared. As for the association's so-called expression of facts, to avoid misunderstandings, it must be explained that if users support the directors' compromise proposal or the proposal of the Telephone Issue Committee, when the telephone company absolutely does not change its attitude, the fact of "not using" should be used to make the telephone company realize its error. Facts are better than words, and reality is the golden rule. In short, if the association encounters any entrustment from users, it will fulfill its responsibilities and strive to the utmost, and will never "shirk responsibility."

Post Office Replies to Telephone Association The Postal Administration replied to the Telephone Issue Committee stating, "Your letter of the 25th of this month has been received and duly noted. After review, your requests to organize communication vehicles and print communication cards, with a uniform fee of one cent each, conflict with the bureau's operations and are not feasible. Your members can use postal postcards for communication within the city. Each postcard is charged only one cent within the city and is delivered according to the ordinary delivery schedule. If faster delivery is required, postcards or letters can be sent as regular express mail. Each item will be charged an additional five cents for regular express fees (regular express postcards within the city cost a total of six cents including postage, and letters cost seven cents. The envelope should be marked '平快 [Regular Express]'). The bureau will arrange for a mail carrier to deliver them according to the express mail delivery schedule to ensure speed. A corresponding reply is hereby provided for your information."

Public Opinion of the City Federation District branches 5, 7, 15, 24, 25, 36, 38, 39 of the Special District Citizens' Federation jointly sent a letter to the Special District Telephone Issue Committee yesterday, stating: "Having seen in the newspapers that the Chinese Taxpayers' Association has indicated that the new Shanghai Telephone Company fees are sufficient for users' needs, this Committee believes that this action is self-contradictory. Therefore, this letter is a rebuttal and proposes to schedule a meeting to announce its dissolution and inform users that if they have any requests in the future, they can directly consult the Association, etc. Your Committee is organized by various groups in the city, with the will of the public as its guide and the pursuit of public interest as its premise, not for the private views of individuals. Moreover, the Public Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association is the general organization of taxpayers in the special district, entrusted by citizens to participate in the 工部局administrative affairs and represent the taxpayers' views in negotiations. Its every word and action has a significant impact. Instead of striving to expand forward, it has put unfounded words into writing. This Association, etc., regrets this very much. Therefore, we jointly urge your Committee to continue its past spirit, fight to the end, uphold the spirit of dauntless sacrifice, and bravely move forward to fight for the users of the city. Our Association, etc., is willing to be your backup. As for announcing dissolution, we will not agree to it until victory is achieved. We urge all members to do their best to overcome the difficulties in order to achieve thorough success. We deeply hope for this."

The Guangdong-Guangxi Industrial Inspection Group Held a Cadre Meeting Yesterday Huang Xuchu Sent a Telegram of Welcome The City Chamber of Commerce Hosted a Reception Last Night 107

The Guangdong-Guangxi Industrial Inspection Group convened a second cadre meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday. More than twenty people attended, including Cai Shengbai, Pan Yangyao, Xiang Kangyuan, Fang Jiange, Hu Xiyuan, Wu Yunqi, Wang Zhisheng, Mao Heyuan, Du Bingshou, Xie Jishan, Shi Gengyin, and Wu Qingtai. Cai Shengbai chaired the meeting. The following resolutions were made as a result of the discussion:

Regarding the transportation of members' luggage, it was resolved that:

a) Those entrusting the association to send luggage must deliver it to the association before 12:00 PM on the third.

b) Those entrusting China Travel Service to send luggage must contact the service to arrange pickup before 5:00 PM on the third.

c) Those carrying luggage themselves should bring it when boarding the ship.

Regarding the boarding time, it was resolved that the ship will set sail at 2:30 AM on the third. Members are required to board a small boat at the Xinguang Pier by 10:30 PM on the afternoon of the third.

Regarding the scheduling of another plenary meeting of all members, it was resolved that it will be held at 3:00 PM on the second to distribute badges, etc. If members are unable to attend, they must send representatives.

Regarding the gift of toothpaste and toothbrushes from the Family Industry Cooperative, it was resolved that a letter of thanks will be sent.

Welcome from Guizhou Governor Huang Xuchu, the chairman of the Guangxi Provincial Government, sent a telegram to the group yesterday to express his welcome. The original telegram is recorded as follows: "Respectfully, Mr. Guo Shun, Chairman of the Shanghai Chinese Industrial Federation, upon reading your telegram, I learned that gentlemen are the backbone of the industry, coming together to guide us from afar. Awaiting enlightenment with utmost welcome. Huang Xuchu respectfully bows, frugal."

Chamber of Commerce Reception At 3:00 PM, the City Chamber of Commerce hosted a reception for all members of the group. More than twenty people attended, accompanied by Yu Zuoting, Chairman of the Chamber, and Zhu Boyuan, Secretary. First, Chairman Yu gave a speech, saying, "The Guangdong-Guangxi Industrial Inspection Group is organized by industrial and commercial magnates of this city and will depart from Shanghai on the fourth of next month. Our Chamber, as the collective body of all merchants in the city, regards the mission of your group with a sense of shared destiny and holds great expectations. Therefore, as you are about to depart, we have prepared some refreshments and invited you to attend to express our farewell sentiments. Your presence is deeply gratifying. There are many reasons for the industrial and commercial decline in our city in recent years, but the gradual shrinking of the market is the most fatal wound. The four northeastern provinces are completely closed off, and even Jiangsu Province is gradually becoming a situation where guests overshadow the hosts. In Guangdong and Guangxi provinces, Shanghai merchants suffer not only from the failure to abolish disguised likin but also from the industrial control of provincial self-government, so that Shanghai factories can only confine themselves to the corner of Central China. This is currently the biggest issue. Regarding taxation, the exemption of grain surtaxes in Guangdong Province is still under unresolved request, and the special tax on leather products has followed suit. In Guangxi Province, products that are usually exempt from heavy taxation for imitating machine-made foreign styles, such as domestic electric fans, must also pay the so-called supplementary tax. Repeated legal disputes have not yet been resolved. Regarding industrial control, most of the larger-scale industries in Guangdong Province are state-owned, so Shanghai factories have little room to compete with similar products in Guangdong, such as cement. However, Guangdong Province on the one hand vigorously implements industrial control of provincial self-government, and on the other hand opposes the 'overall, systematic, and planned national industrial control.' Our Chamber has sent a letter to the province asking it to explain the reasons for its opposition, but we have not received a reply. During your trip today, you must openly discuss with officials and businessmen in the province to find ways to overcome these difficulties, so that Shanghai's commercial opportunities will be restored. In other words, this is originally the responsibility of our Chamber, but in recent years, relying solely on commercial requests in writing has been ineffective. We have no choice but to entrust you with this important task on the occasion of your southern tour. We hope that you will understand our sincere intentions."

Mr. Cai's reply It was decided that Cai Shengbai, the head of the inspection group, would give the reply, "Our group's trip to the south today, receiving the hospitality of your Chamber and the guidance of the chairman, is a great honor. The purpose of our trip is to open up domestic goods sales. Because the sales channels in Guangdong and Guangxi are very broad, we will investigate the local situation, to learn and use it as a reference for improvement. We will investigate domestic raw materials to promote their use and connect the emotions of the two places to jointly promote domestic goods. Where our capabilities are insufficient, we still need your Chamber's assistance and guidance." At 2:00 PM on the afternoon of the second, the Chinese Industrial Federation will host a reception for the group. At the same time, the Citizens' Domestic Goods Association Sports Meeting will also host all members. At 7:00 PM, Yang Dezhao will also host a farewell banquet.

Mayor's Speech

Mayor Wu delivered the opening address, saying, "Esteemed committee members, esteemed guests, today our association is holding the opening ceremony of the Pushan Road, Damuqiao Road, Qimei Road, and Zhongshan Road Common People's New Villages. I am very grateful for the presence of people from all walks of life in this city. At the same time, due to time and space constraints, I have been unable to guide everyone to visit each village one by one, and I must express my considerable apologies. However, the facilities and tasks undertaken by the four Common People's Villages are roughly the same. You can get an overall sense from looking at just one of them. I hope that everyone will provide more guidance after visiting this village. The primary task of our society's construction is the people's livelihood. And among the people's livelihood's necessities of clothing, food, housing, and transportation, housing is the most urgent problem. In this city, shantytowns stand side by side, and factories are densely packed. The general poor citizens feel the pain of not being able to live in peace, and therefore cannot develop an interest in working happily. Our association was established to meet this need. We have painstakingly operated over the past year, adding four new Common People's Villages. The purpose is to solve the housing problem so that ordinary poor and working-class citizens will not suffer under the highly competitive conditions of urban life. However, there are a large number of common people who cannot live in peace and work happily. A mere four villages with only a few hundred houses are of limited capacity and can be said to be only a very small contribution from our association to society. It is certainly not enough to meet the needs of the common people. This is only the beginning of social undertakings. We feel the gravity of the mission we bear and see the depth and magnitude of the suffering endured by the common people. With regard to the smallest achievements of the past year, we can only increase our belief in serving society and move forward. Recently, our association has been planning to build a new labor village and is studying various other plans in order to gradually implement them. We hope to make a greater contribution to society, especially to the common people. There are passive and active aspects to social welfare work. For example, the rent regulations in our association's villages are very low, in order to reduce the burden on the common people. This belongs to the passive aspect. The residents of each village are mostly poor people, and in fact, they can represent the common people of this city. Their expectations of the government are very high. The above-mentioned passive work is only to give them a slight respite. In terms of welfare, it still depends on the efforts of active work. Therefore, the task of our association is to focus on improving the lives of the common people and providing them with all kinds of necessary training to make them good citizens. During the construction of the Common People's New Villages, our association spent hundreds of thousands of yuan. The purpose we hold is not only limited to passively reducing the burden on the common people, but also to actively engage in the construction of education, health, and social undertakings. If you examine the facilities of this village, you will know the general idea. Now, most of the residents of each village have moved in. Taking this village as an example, all 330 residential buildings have been fully occupied. This proves the urgent need of the common people for government assistance. At the same time, our association also feels the need to continue to strive to serve the common people. The young people working in each village have all received training from our association, and they all have a strong desire to serve society. We believe that under the leadership and guidance of our association, they will be able to understand their responsibilities and work hard on the positive work that the common people urgently need. Our goal is to achieve the ability of the residents of the new villages to live and work in peace in the future and to receive appropriate civic training so that they can exercise their four rights, and further unite to become a model citizens' group. Therefore, the facilities of the welfare undertakings of each village are completely based on Sun Yat-sen's Three People's Principles. Although there are no achievements to speak of today, we have infinite hopes for the future of the villagers. However, social undertakings should be completed by the joint efforts of people from all walks of life. Relying solely on the strength of the government is unlikely to achieve much success. In the past year, our association has spent a great deal of money, but the development of the undertakings in each village and the measures for the welfare undertakings of the common people outside each village still require the expenditure of large amounts of funds. At a time when the government's finances are difficult, it is not easy to seek to benefit all the common people in this city. We hope that people from all walks of life will cooperate with the government and provide sympathetic assistance."

Advisor's Speech

Dalonglian, the Western advisor of the Zhongshan Road Common People's Village, then gave a speech, first expressing his honor at participating in the opening ceremony of the Common People's Village. He then said that there are many common people living in simple houses with poor environments in the suburbs of Shanghai, which affects their health and will affect the entire city of Shanghai. Fortunately, Mayor Wu advocated the Common People's New Village so that the common people can have well-equipped residences. He hopes that there will be greater success in the future.

Hongming's Speech

Hongming, the representative of the Chinese Buddhist Association, wearing a blue robe, went to the rostrum, put his hands together, and began his speech, briefly saying that Mayor Wu of this city, with his usual care for the common people, had painstakingly planned and today has finally completed it. The cleanliness of its layout, the abundance of air and light, and the conformity of its internal management to the new era will benefit the common people in the future. It is by no means a small achievement. I am honored to participate in this grand ceremony and see this great cause, and I dare to be sincere in praising and eulogizing Mayor Wu, wishing him boundless blessings and longevity.

Residents' Speech of Thanks

Xu Jiazhi, the representative of the residents, gave a speech of thanks, briefly saying that, because of the difficulty of life, we were terrified about the problem of housing in Shanghai, where land is so expensive. Not only are the prices expensive, but the poor environment makes us feel pain everywhere in our lives. We rely on Mayor Wu and the committee members to care about the hardships of the common people, to think for us, and to build this Common People's Village. Its low price, the abundance of air and light, and the cleanliness of its layout are vastly different from the past. Our children can enjoy compulsory education, and patients can receive free medical care. The purchase of daily necessities is also cheaper than outside. Everything can give us material and spiritual comfort and pleasure. We are grateful for this great kindness and will never forget the virtuous administration of Mayor Wu and the committee members. There was also a resident representative who was nearly ten years old, named Huang Shenhua, who used his clever tone to give a brief speech of thanks, expressing his gratitude for Mayor Wu's virtuous administration.

Awarding Ceremony

The last was the awarding ceremony of the first class of graduates of the Service Personnel Training Class of the Common People's Welfare Association. First, Committee Member Jian Youwen gave a report, briefly saying that when this association was planning to build the Common People's Village, Mayor Wu intended to start a service personnel training class in order to ensure strict management. Therefore, he began recruiting students last year. All applicants were graduates of universities and secondary schools. After four and a half months of training, they had three months of internship. Each student was very interested in this matter and handled it very seriously. They will definitely benefit the common people in the future.

Graduates

After Committee Member Jian finished his report, Mayor Wu awarded the certificates. The recipients included Li Putian, Yan Guodong, Zai Chongde, Wang Zufufu (director), Yang Jianwen, Xu Guanren, Zheng Jiabi, and Hu Xiufang from Pushan Road Common People's Village; Liu Xiang, Lu Shiqi, Chao Ruisheng (director), Li Derong, Shu Wen, Chen Zhenying, and Zhang Xiuhe from Damuqiao Road Common People's Village; Shen Hua, Zhang Jilin, Li Caihua, Yang Fugen, Liu Boyuan, Li Xingnan (director), Zhang Xipi, Wu Xueyi, and Qu Tong from Qimei Road Common People's Village; and Hong Xiaonong (director), Liu Yaozhen, Zheng Guisheng, Lu Dingyi, Han Yongsheng, Wang Junshan, Zhou Xiang, Zhao Liansheng, Yan Zigang, Chen Yi, and Chen Silin from Zhongshan Road Common People's Village.

Room Arrangement

All the houses in the Zhongshan Road Common People's Village are south-facing bungalows, totaling 330 rooms. Every six rooms are a group, and every two groups are a row. The rooms are spacious and have the preparation for a small garden. In the middle is a wide cement avenue. The interiors have cement floors, and the width and depth are both more than one foot. There are also stairs to climb to the attic, where two tatami mats can be accommodated. In the back, there are two small rooms, one for storing boxes and luggage, and one for the kitchen. The air and light are sufficient.

Public Facilities

There are now more than 150 families who have moved into the Zhongshan Road New Village, so various undertakings have begun to be carried out. According to reports from the Central News Agency, the village already has a complete primary school, an adult supplementary school, and a women's supplementary school. All residents are enrolled in schools. There is also a clinic, a public tea garden, and a consumer cooperative, all of which have been opened. In addition, men's and women's showers and men's and women's toilets have been built, and the layout is very clean. In the center of the village, there is a sports field that occupies a fairly large area, providing residents with extracurricular activities. There are also plans to organize extracurricular entertainment for residents and engage in side jobs. There are still more than one hundred houses that have been rented out and will be moved in soon. The grand occasion of the Common People's New Village. (Photo by International Press)

Recruitment Bureau Staff: Screening Results Announced Yesterday; 55 Passed the Exam, 58 Publicly Dismissed 110

Since the state-run Recruitment Bureau held written examinations for all its staff on the 23rd of last month, the test papers and work performance reports were taken to Nanjing by Deputy Manager Lao Mian to request the Ministry of Transportation's approval regarding which staff should be dismissed and retained. Only yesterday morning did he return to Shanghai, and the list of dismissed staff was announced by the General Manager at 4 PM. The details are as follows:

Lao Mian Returns from Beijing

The standard for determining dismissals remained the quality of writing in the examination as the criterion for retention or dismissal. Earlier, the Ministry sent a telegram to Cai Zengji, ordering him to go to Beijing to discuss this matter, but Cai, due to his busy schedule, sent Lao Mian instead. Therefore, the test papers and work performance reports of all staff were taken together. Deputy Manager Lao consulted with Acting Minister Yu in Beijing for several days before a decision was made. The standard for passing or failing was based on the scores of oral and written examinations. Lao Mian returned to Shanghai from Beijing yesterday morning. The Bureau first paid the staff salaries for February in the morning. Because it was the end of the month, the dismissal list was decided and announced in the afternoon, and all department staff were ordered to remain at the Bureau to await the announcement.

Manager Convenes a Meeting

Yesterday was Saturday, and normally a day of rest in the afternoon. All staff were usually free to leave. Deputy Manager Tan specifically notified all section chiefs in advance not to leave and to remain at the Bureau. Around 3 PM, he would convene a meeting with the staff of each section to announce the list of those dismissed and retained and to discuss the redistribution of work for those who remained. It was not until 3:30 PM that the two Deputy Managers, Tan and Lao, summoned the staff to the Board of Directors to make the announcement, stating that the list of retained staff had been approved by the Ministry of Transportation, totaling 55 people (excluding the accounting section and technical personnel). They were ordered to redistribute their duties according to the list. This dismissal decision still emphasized the written examination, and those with better writing skills were retained. Their work performance was not considered. Many individuals with outstanding achievements were not selected. Only 55 staff members passed the examination. The number of dismissed staff already announced was 34 from the Business Department, 8 from the Shipping Department, 14 from the General Affairs Department, and 2 from the Treasury. The Accounting Department has not yet been announced. A total of 58 staff members were officially dismissed yesterday. In addition, 6 staff members from the Business Department voluntarily resigned and were also approved.

List of Retained Staff

The list of retained staff is as follows: Business Department (including the Warehouse Section and Joint Transport Section) originally had over 70 people, now only 35 remain, including Yun Zhi, Li Sixun, Chen Xuliang, Wang Heqing, He Quansheng, Tao Futang, Wu Delin, Jin Duo, Gao Hanruo, Dai Buzhou, Zhang Shousun, Chen Yuhua, Wang Shengliang, Tang Xie, Zou Lun, Xu Yulin, Xu Guoyuan, Qian Xiangchu, Fei Jiasheng, Lin Jiehou, Wang Yuhuai, Hong Yansheng, Yao Shushen, Lu Zhaoxun, Guo Jingsu, Shen Shaosheng, Ye Yuan, Wang Xianqi, He Yueming, and trainees Jiang Jiaxiang, Sheng Qiqiao, Zhang Shengrong, Zhu Zengxiang, Wu Renlin. Shipping Department retained Qian Mingshu, Li Rui, Gong Jinglun, Shen Jianbao, Ye Yanhong, Jiang Weishan, Li Weilan, Qin Zuyin, Li Wenhua, and interns Ye Shiyi and Tang Ying, who were not included in the examination. The Treasury retained Yu Tianjue and four others. The Accounting Department will be handled separately.

Severance Pay to be Collected Tomorrow

The 56 staff members dismissed from the three departments and the two staff members from the Treasury will receive three months of severance pay and four months of accumulated double salary (totaling six months' salary). This salary could not be paid out yesterday and has been scheduled for payment on Monday. However, because of the large number of dismissals in the Business Department, it is felt that there are too few people left to handle the work of signing and issuing bills of lading, recording books, and other tasks in the general office (only two of the original seventeen people remain). The heads of each section are requesting instructions from Tan Boying and Lao Mian on how to handle this situation.

Creditors Win Lawsuit After Closure of Hong Kong National Bank; Bank's Objection to Jurisdiction Rejected by Court; Ordered to Pay in Full Plus Late Interest 113

Since the closure of the Hong Kong National Bank, creditors of the Shanghai branch have applied to the court for the bank's bankruptcy. However, the bank submitted an accounting statement proving that the amount owed by debtors was sufficient to cover the debts and more, and the court determined that bankruptcy was not appropriate. The creditors were very pleased and waited patiently for the return of their deposits. However, because the bank had been closed for a long time and was very secretive about the liquidation process, the creditor Zhang Yaorui and others, believing that abandoning the debt for so long was not a long-term solution, entrusted lawyer Liang Yaobing to file a lawsuit with the Shanghai First Special District District Court to recover the deposits. The court has now ruled in favor of the plaintiffs and ordered the Hong Kong National Bank to pay back the plaintiffs' deposits in full, plus late interest. The reasons for the court's judgment are excerpted as follows: "The defendant shall pay the plaintiffs Zhang Yaorui and others their deposits, plus interest until the date of execution, and the litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant." The defendant and its legal representative stated that the court had no jurisdiction and requested that the plaintiff's lawsuit be dismissed. Their defense stated that the defendant was a branch of the Hong Kong National Savings Bank, which was registered with the British government in Hong Kong. Although the defendant was registered with the Chinese Ministry of Industry, it was still a British legal person and not subject to the jurisdiction of this court. Therefore, they requested that the plaintiff's lawsuit be dismissed, presenting the registration certificate from the British Consulate General in Shanghai and the registration certificate from the Chinese Ministry of Industry as evidence. The court ruled that the Shanghai branch of the Hong Kong National Savings Bank, the defendant in this case, was established with the approval of the Chinese Ministry of Industry on April 3, 20th year of the Republic of China and issued a registration certificate. By applying to the Chinese government for approval of its establishment, it indicated its willingness to enjoy the same rights and obligations as Chinese legal persons of the same type and to be subject to Chinese law. According to Article 12 of the Implementation Law of the General Principles of the Civil Code, this court should have jurisdiction over the defendant. Based on the above, the plaintiff's lawsuit is justified, and the judgment is made in accordance with Article 78 of the Civil Procedure Law as stated in the main text."

Foreign Vessel Aground Near Majiakou in the Yangtze River Sends Distress Signal; New Vessel Runs Aground Again After Rescue from Wuxue 114

In the Yangtze River waterway near Gaozi, upstream from Zhenjiang, the Tai Gu Company's new Yangtze River vessel Wuxue, which had run aground last year and was rescued after several months, was rescued and returned to Shanghai the day before yesterday. It was scheduled to be inspected today and resume service next Wednesday. However, at noon yesterday, this port received a wireless telegraph stating that a foreign merchant vessel (name unknown) had run aground near Gaozi after the pilot mistakenly entered the waterway and sailed into a shallow area near Dear Island. The location is near a paper mill and directly opposite Majiakou. The vessel's hull is stuck in the shallow sand and cannot move. It is currently sending out distress signals.

Emergency Loan of 500,000 Yuan Fully Repaid 115

According to Da Gong She, the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Disaster Relief in Various Provinces, in order to provide emergency relief for the flood disasters in Hubei, Shandong, Hunan, Jiangsu, Jiangxi, Henan, and Anhui provinces last August, borrowed 500,000 yuan from the Central Bank, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and 28 other banks. At that time, the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications agreed to lend 300,000 yuan, and the remaining 200,000 yuan was entrusted to the Shanghai Banking Association to borrow from its member banks. The 28 banks each contributed amounts ranging from 1,000 to 10,000 yuan. In addition to the agreement signed by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, each of the other banks signed individual agreements for record-keeping. The interest rate was set at 7% per annum, but the repayment period was not specified. The Association promised to repay the loans as soon as possible from the disaster relief funds donated by various parties. By the end of last year, half of the loans had been repaid from the donations deposited into the Central Bank. Yesterday, the person in charge of the Association's finance group told a Da Gong She reporter that the 500,000 yuan emergency relief loan borrowed from the banks had been fully repaid by the end of February of this year, using the disaster relief funds collected. All agreements have been returned and canceled. Among them, 160,000 yuan was the amount obtained by the Association from the Ministry of Finance using the 24-year disaster relief public bonds allocated by the Disaster Relief Committee to the Association and then converted to cash at the Bank of China.

Degrades China

Third Phase of Railway Bonds Issued Today; Zhang Gongquan Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning; Discussed Issuance Matters with the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications; Scheduled to Visit the Yuehan Railway in Wuhan Tomorrow 117

The first 40 million yuan of the third phase of railway construction bonds issued by the Ministry of Railways will be issued today. Minister Zhang Gongquan arrived in Shanghai from Beijing yesterday morning to discuss issuance matters with the banking community and is scheduled to visit the Yuehan Railway in Wuhan on the 2nd. The details are as follows:

40 Million Yuan Issued Today

The Ministry of Railways is issuing 120 million yuan of the third phase of railway construction bonds in three installments to build trunk lines such as Xiangqian, Chuanggui, and to subsidize existing lines such as PingSui, Zhengtai, Jiaoji, and to extend existing routes. The first installment will be issued on March 1, 25th year, the second installment on March 1, 26th year, and the third installment on March 1, 27th year. The annual interest rate is set at 6%, and the surplus profits from the construction and extension of new lines and the surplus profits from other state-owned railways, excluding existing debt repayments, are designated as the fund and managed by a management committee. The bonds will be issued at 98% of their face value and divided into three denominations: 1,000 yuan, 500 yuan, and 100 yuan.

Discuss Issuance, Inspect Yuehan

Minister of Railways Zhang Gongquan arrived in Shanghai from Beijing yesterday morning to discuss the issuance of the first 40 million yuan of the third phase of railway construction bonds with the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications. The underwriting is handled by these three banks, and the mortgaging of cash to various banks is still awaiting a decision from Minister Zhang in consultation with the banking community. It is reported that Zhang will leave Shanghai for Hankou on March 2 to inspect the Yuehan Railway and will return to Beijing after arriving in Guangdong.

Shanghai Yesterday: Spring Cold Like Midwinter; Northwest Wind Howled, Pedestrians Shivered; Thin Ice Formed on the Sea Off Daji Mountain 120

The weather in this city has been like midwinter for the past few days, an unusual phenomenon for springtime in recent years. The northwest wind has been howling all day long, piercing the skin, and even more so in the morning and evening. Pedestrians shiver, huffing and puffing. Moreover, there was another sudden snowfall the day before yesterday, leading to a proliferation of diseases, and throat ailments and colds are easily transmitted. At the same time, it is difficult for crops such as wheat, vegetables, and beans planted in the four rural areas to grow, so the market price of vegetables has been rising for several days. Unexpectedly, the cold was even more severe yesterday. At 5 AM, the sky was overcast, and water turned to ice. Ditches and water pipes were almost all frozen. Even indoors, it was impossible to stay warm without fur. It was not until around 9 AM that sunlight appeared, but it was still intermittent, and snowflakes were seen. Only at noon did the red sun appear in the sky, bringing a little warmth. However, after noon, the weather turned cold again. In the evening, the cold air was even more intense, like midwinter weather. According to the report from the local weather station, the lowest temperature yesterday was 26.1 degrees, and the highest was 36.5 degrees. Unless the southeast wind turns around, it will be difficult to ease the cold for a while. Therefore, the general rural population is worried, as the spring planting is difficult, and the vegetables that have already been planted have been damaged by the ice. Everyone is worried that if it does not warm up again, it will affect the harvest. What is even stranger is that thin ice even formed on the sea off the coast of Wusongkou outside Daji Mountain yesterday, and it only melted around 9 AM.

Domestically Produced Cigarette Paper Successfully Developed; Samples to be Given Away Starting Today; National Cigarette Factories Will Be Happy to Use It 121

According to Shiye She, the quality of domestic cigarettes has been improving day by day in recent years, and they can compete with foreign goods. However, cigarette wrapping paper has never been domestically produced and has always been imported, resulting in alarming annual losses. In view of this, the Minfeng Paper Mill has devoted itself to research and manufacturing and has been successful. It will soon be available on the market. In addition to the Minfeng Factory, the China Factory at No. 695 Tiantong An Road, Zhabei, has also recently successfully developed cigarette paper and will be giving away samples starting today. It will be available for sale at the beginning of next month. The factory issued an announcement yesterday stating, "In view of the fact that all cigarette wrapping paper required by domestic cigarette companies across the country is imported, resulting in annual losses of over four million yuan, this factory purchased machinery and established a factory last year to research and manufacture it. It was successfully developed on January 1 of this year and is no less superior than imported products. This factory plans to open soon. From the standpoint of domestic goods, cigarette factories across the country will be happy to purchase this product. In addition to submitting the product for registration with the Ministry of Industry and filing with the Social Bureau, a public announcement is hereby made, hoping that purely domestic cigarette factories everywhere will come to request samples."

The Case of Clifford, General Manager of the American Asiatic Bank: Facts Clarified After Third Court Hearing, Yesterday Commenced Oral Arguments, Hearing Adjourned and Bail Continued 122

The case of German national Clifford, the General Manager of the defunct American Asiatic Bank, accused of privately converting cash entrusted to the bank for safekeeping by depositors into notification deposits, thereby causing losses to the depositors, has been heard for the third time by the Chief Judge of the Criminal Division of the First Special District Court, Qian Hongye, who summoned the defendant and a group of individuals, thoroughly investigating and clarifying the facts.

Facts Clarified, Arguments Commenced

Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, the lawyers for both sides were instructed to present oral arguments in the First Tribunal. First, the lawyers for the plaintiff, the Public Works Department, Liang Rubao and Bao Yi, one speaking in English and the other translating, presented the reasons why the defendant should be held liable. This lasted for over an hour. The gist of their argument was that the collapse of the American Asiatic Bank was like a puppet show. The compradore of the bank, Huang Yicai, and the head of the custody department, Zhu Yousong, were merely puppets, while the defendant Clifford was the mastermind pulling the strings behind the scenes. The play could be called "The Failure of the American Asiatic Bank." Examining the reasons for the failure, it was neither due to a market downturn nor did it involve other issues; it was purely due to the defendant's fraud, embezzlement, and breach of trust. The American Asiatic Bank was not registered with the Chinese government.

Partnership Nature, General Manager Responsible

It can only be recognized as a partnership, and the General Manager should bear full responsibility. He cannot shirk responsibility for all the actions of the bank by claiming ignorance. The points that the plaintiff needs to prove are: 1. The defendant was the General Manager; 2. There were illegal activities; 3. The American Asiatic Bank gained illegal benefits from these illegal activities. Now, all three points have been definitively proven. Furthermore, Yang Xiqing came to court and detailed the process of his contacting the compradore Huang Yicai to deposit 20,000 in cash for safekeeping. The testimonies of Huang Yicai and Zhu Yousong are also consistent with Yang's, disproving any claims that Yang, Huang, and Zhu are lying. Although the defendant and Huang were initially very close, since the case began, the defendant has attacked Huang in court. However, the defendant should have foreseen this type of crime by Huang. The testimony of Leventhal, who was presented by the defendant,

Leventhal Should be Held Liable for Embezzlement

Leventhal's talent and knowledge are indeed excellent. He was able to overdraw huge amounts of money from the bank unconditionally and invest it in speculative ventures. His character can be inferred from this. As someone in charge of safekeeping, how could he not have personally seen the 20,000 in cash and yet rashly sign the receipt? If he were to be held responsible, he could hardly escape the crime of embezzlement in his duties. Moreover, the bank's regulations stated that employees could not open overdraft accounts. He once pointed out Huang Yicai's illegal actions, but his own crime was actually greater than Huang's. Therefore, Leventhal's testimony is not credible.

Excessive Lending Does Not Comply with Bank Rules

The bank's regulations stipulate that lending should not exceed one-tenth of the capital. Its capital was 2.5 million, but the loan to Hexing Company alone reached 2.5 million, exhausting all the funds. There was also a loan of 1.16 million to Puyi Company, and other loans of several hundred thousand were not insignificant. The reason for the excessive lending was that Leventhal was the chairman of Hexing Company, and other debtors, such as Puyi, had close ties with him. Therefore, they no longer considered the harm to the bank itself.

Both Chinese and American Laws are Not Compliant

For example, Huang Yicai owed more than 100,000, and his collateral was the bank's stock. This is non-compliant under both Chinese and American laws. The bank not only allowed Leventhal to take whatever he wanted, but also allowed many of Leventhal's relatives to overdraw, treating the American Asiatic Bank as Leventhal's private property. The defendant also engaged in speculation. The reason why he did not owe money but had 27,000 deposited in the bank was that he benefited from the bank's economic turnover. With this backing, he was able to turn defeat into victory. Although his deposit was also lost when the bank failed, what he gained was enough to compensate for his losses. Since the case began, the defendant knew that he was in a disadvantageous position and tried to persuade Huang to reconcile with Yang, believing that returning the money to Yang would lead to the withdrawal of the lawsuit. Now there is an attached civil suit. If the defendant is judged to be responsible for repayment, the liquidation office can suffer less loss.

Hoff's Words are Not Without Bias

However, the testimony of the liquidator Hoff is not without bias, and his words whitewashed the defendant. This actually exceeded his authority and amounted to a breach of trust, which should be noted. After the bank collapsed, a depositor committed suicide. In his suicide note, he stated that all his life's savings had vanished, and he took his own life out of grief and indignation. This kind of tragic case of family ruin was caused by the bank. The defendant, as the General Manager, should indeed bear the blame and be brought to justice, etc.

Defendant Has Three Lawyers Defending Him

The defendant's lawyers then presented their defense. There were three lawyers defending him. First, lawyer Chen Tingrui stated that the police handling the case, from the investigation on the 17th to the arguments on the 17th, repeatedly used smoke bombs, creating a tense and thick atmosphere. After the collapse of the American Asiatic Bank, those who were affected and lost their families and those who died were indeed very unfortunate. However, the collapse of the bank is one thing, and whether the defendant committed a crime is another. One cannot hold the General Manager fully responsible simply because he was the General Manager of a collapsed bank.

Bank Failures are Common

Moreover, in recent years, bank failures have been common. It has never been heard of to blame the president of the bank alone. The Shanghai Municipal Council's punishment of Leventhal and Baron was because Leventhal and Baron had committed crimes. The defendant's position and the facts of the case are different from Leventhal and Baron. The police cannot use Leventhal and Baron as examples and draw analogies. To say that the defendant intended to have Huang Yicai reconcile with Yang Xiqing is to recognize that the defendant was acting out of fear of crime. This is merely speculation and is not credible. Now, regarding the facts of the case, that is, the cash safekeeping being changed to notification deposit, this is truly undisputed by both parties. What needs to be studied is only the question of whether the defendant should be held responsible for this matter. The police believe that the defendant, as the General Manager, must have known about the change in the name of the deposit.

Extensive Scope, Unavoidably Demanding

It must be known that the American Asiatic Bank had a very extensive scope, with nearly a hundred employees, and deposits and withdrawals of around 50 million every day. It is difficult for the defendant to personally handle every detail. If his subordinates have illegal behavior, it is unavoidable to demand that the chief executive be responsible. Moreover, the criminal law stipulates that there should be no implications. Although there was a law in ancient times that one person's crime would affect the entire family, this is not the case in modern times. If the police can prove with documentary evidence and witness testimony that the defendant did indeed participate in criminal behavior, then the defendant should bear the blame. However, none of the photos, books, notification deposit receipts, or the receipts held by Yang and Yi were signed by the defendant.

The Words of Huang and Zhu are Indeed Credible

As for the testimony of witnesses, apart from the facts stated by Yang Xiqing, Huang Yicai and Zhu Yousong are of the same ilk. Huang, as the compradore of the American Asiatic Bank, had his contract witnessed by Zhu, and Zhu owed Huang more than 5,000. The relationship between the two is certainly not ordinary. How could Zhu not be Huang's echo? Huang, having obtained illegal benefits, wants to shift the blame to the defendant. Therefore, such testimony is indeed credible. Huang often argued that he had to obey the General Manager's orders because of the contract stipulations. However, the contract stated that obedience was only for legal orders. Is privately changing the name of the deposit a legal act? Moreover, the accounts between the compradores on April 8th of last year have been investigated. The amount deposited on that day increased by 20,000. This should undoubtedly be the 20,000 in cash delivered by Yang Xiqing.

Changing the Name of the Deposit was Done in the Same Way

Later, when Huang saw that changing the name of Yang's deposit was going smoothly, he still instructed Zhu to do the same for Yi Xiede's safekeeping deposit. Although Zhu did not gain any benefit, as Huang's debtor, he naturally obeyed his orders. The liquidator Hoff had already truly seen through this, so his testimony in court was fair and did not favor the defendant at all. In short, since the defendant was not the perpetrator of illegal acts and the bank did not obtain illegal benefits, he should not bear any responsibility, etc. The time had reached noon, so Chief Judge Qian adjourned the hearing until next Monday and ordered that the defendant Clifford remain on bail.

Murder of Feng Zhang, Suspect Nephew Zhu Er, Neighbors Discover and Report to Police 123

Feng Zhang, a woman from Nanhui, Pudong, was 40 years old. Her husband had died many years ago, and she had some savings. She currently lived at number 94 near Xiaoputuo Bridge, outside Xiaonanmen, Nanshi. She had a nephew named Zhu Er, who had no steady job and associated with hooligans. Unexpectedly, the afternoon before yesterday, Zhu Er suddenly came to her house with a man, claiming to visit his aunt. They then went into her room to talk. At the time, the neighbors did not pay much attention because they knew that Zhu Er was her nephew. Until yesterday morning at about 10:00 AM, when the sun was high, the neighbors still did not see her get up. So they went into her bedroom to check and suddenly saw her lying on the bed, her face pale and blood foaming from her mouth. They touched her body and it was cold, she had been dead for a long time. Her nephew Zhu Er and the man who came with him were nowhere to be found. So they rushed to inform her husband's brother, Feng Zhilin, (who works as a gatekeeper in Jiuji Lumber Company in Nanshi) who, after seeing the situation, immediately reported it to the Dongjiadu Police Station, asking for justice. Chief Yi, after receiving the report, immediately sent police officers to investigate. They also found fresh blood flowing from her lower body. The bedding on the bed was stained with blood. The clothes chests in her room were also open, and the contents had been ransacked and scattered on the ground, clearly having been turned over by someone. There were no obvious wounds on her body, so the details of the case are quite bizarre. Because the case involved a human life, the chief immediately instructed the local headman to report to the Shanghai Local Court. The Chief Prosecutor immediately sent Prosecutor Li Zhulin to investigate. After examining the scene and determining that the deceased had indeed died from poisoning, he sent a large number of detectives to investigate the truth and arrest the murderer to bring him to justice.

Fire on Tongfu Road Yesterday Morning: Nine People Injured Jumping from Building 135

Fashion Company Fire Late at Night, Stairwell Burns Through, Employees Jump From Windows

According to Datong News Agency, a fire broke out yesterday morning at the Meili Fashion Company, located at 328 Tongfu Road in this city. Because the fire's location was near the stairwell, it burned through in an instant. Nine employees sleeping on the second floor were unable to descend and all jumped from the windows, resulting in injuries to all nine. An investigation into the circumstances follows:

Two Shops Sharing Space

328 Tongfu Road is a double-fronted shop building rented by Huang Jinyan from Pudong. Huang himself opened the Meili Fashion Company in the front section facing the street. The remaining interior of the shop was sublet to Wang Jingbo from Beiping, who opened Renli Antique Silverware Shop. The second floor served as the Meili Garment Factory and the employees' dormitory, housing nine employees in one room. The Renli employees slept in the shop area on the lower level.

Fire Late at Night

Yesterday morning around 3:00 AM, a fire suddenly broke out on the second floor of Meili (some say under the stairwell). At that time, the employees were sound asleep. By the time they noticed, the fire had already spread. Simultaneously, the stairwell connecting the second floor to the first floor had been burned through. The nine Meili employees sleeping on the second floor hastily jumped from the windows to escape, resulting in injuries to all of them. One person reportedly rode a bicycle to the hospital for treatment, hence the rumor of a missing person.

Extinguished After Being Doused

A police officer stationed at the intersection of Jing'an Temple and Tongfu Road noticed smoke billowing out and realized there was a fire. He immediately reported it to the Chengdu Road Police Station and the Central Fire Brigade. Soon, several fire engines arrived and quickly doused the flames, extinguishing the fire. Besides the second floor being destroyed, only the iron awning used to protect the glass window facing the street on the lower floor was pulled down. The rest was intact, and the goods were not damaged. The Chengdu Road Police Station also dispatched a large number of Chinese and foreign officers to maintain order at the scene.

Nine People Injured

Further investigation revealed the names of the employees injured from jumping: Hu Changgeng (19 years old, Pudong), Wang Ahu (16 years old, Pudong), Zhang Renzhong (20 years old, Wuxi), Fang Amao (17 years old, Pudong), Wang Fumin (17 years old, Pudong), Xu Gaoquan (19 years old, Zhejiang), Chen Guichu (20 years old, Jiangsu), Zhang Hai (17 years old, Gaoqiao). (All of the above were sent to Binlong Hospital by the police station in ambulances.) Zheng Longgeng (according to employees of neighboring shops, he hired a car and went to the hospital himself). All of the above suffered injuries to their legs, feet, shoulders, abdomen, etc., but none were life-threatening. It is said that the cause of the fire was due to an electric iron left unswitched off, causing an electrical short.

National Mining Association Held General Meeting of Members Yesterday 138

Resolutions were passed to continue requesting a reduction in the mining product tax and coal tax rates, and to organize the North China Association. The details are recorded below:

Attending Representatives

Those who attended yesterday included Xu Ziyi from Datong Jinbei Mining Bureau, Lu Bingru from Yangquan Baojin Mining Company, Dai Linshu from Shanghai Huadong Coal Mining Company, Zhang Zhongping and Wang Zimin from Zhongxing Coal Mining Company, Zhu Yonghe and Xia Liangda from Datong Coal Mining Company, Tong Kangling from Pole Coal Mine Company, Meng Xinzhi from Henan Zhongfu Joint Office, Wang Junshi and Sun Tiesheng from Tianjin Kailuan Mining Bureau, Li Zucai from Beiping Yili Coal Mine Company, Zhao Xingchang from Shanghai Hanyeping Company, Liu Wanqing and Li Guangqi from Zhejiang Changxing Coal Mine Company, and new member Wang Zemin from Henan Xing'an Coal Mine Company. Report Items 139

Regarding the request from Yili Company for the association to submit a request to the Ministry of Industry, to be forwarded to the Ministry of Finance, to cancel the estimated high price tax rate for coal in the Hebei, Jin, Chahar, and Suiyuan areas and to temporarily collect taxes at the old rate, the Ministry of Industry forwarded it to the Executive Yuan, which stated that this revision of the Hebei mining product tax was absolutely different from a tax increase and was not approved. Regarding the request from Huadong and Datong companies for the association to request the Ministry of Industry and the Ministry of Railways to implement a uniform special price for coal transportation on the Jinpu Railway, the ministry approved it by telegram. Regarding the application of Anhui Huimei Coal Mine Company to join the association as a member, the Iron and Steel Division of the Ministry of Industry was informed by letter that it could only join after obtaining legal person status. Regarding the government's revision of the tax rate on imported coal from Vietnam last year, the association telegraphed the Executive Yuan and ministries to pay attention. The Executive Yuan replied that this was a settled case and could not be changed, but it had ordered the competent authorities to plan relief measures. Regarding various reports from the Production and Sales Research Committee. Regarding the Ministry of Industry's approval document on measures to ban indigenous methods and unlicensed small mines, the competent authorities had been ordered to handle them. Regarding the Ministry of Railways' approval document on the 15% surcharge on coal and coke freight rates on various railways, it was approved for a six-month extension. Regarding the Executive Yuan's approval document on the request to reduce coal and coke freight rates on the Pinghan Railway. Regarding the survey of simplified domestic mining industry charts printed by various railways. Brief on income and expenditure for 1935.

Discussion Items 140

Previously, the association had sent letters to all public and private members asking them to carefully study the inapplicability and simplicity of the current mining law, to express their opinions, and to send them to the association for review in order to prepare for submitting a proposal to the Legislative Yuan to draft a new mining law. There were opinions from Jie, Baojin, Yili, Liuhegou, etc., each presenting a written proposal. A resolution was made to hand them over to the Board of Directors for preliminary review. Regarding the mining product tax, coal tax rate, and market price standards, repeated requests for reduction had not been approved. A resolution was made for the association to continue requesting the ministry. Regarding the plan to commemorate Mr. Ding Wenjiang, it was resolved that the Geological Survey Institute of the Ministry of Industry already had a plan to commemorate Mr. Ding and that the association should send a letter inviting all fellow companies to join in unity. Latvian Monk Visits China 143

According to the Central News Agency, Venerable Tejsmānanda, a high-ranking monk from Latvia, Europe, and his disciple Ananda, came to China ten days ago to study Buddhism. They are currently residing at the Buddhist Pure Land Society on Hed Road in this city. The monk is 64 years old and has lived the life of a monk for 43 years. His disciple is 24 years old, fluent in ten languages, especially Sanskrit and Tibetan. They both specialize in Esoteric Buddhism and have studied in Tibet and Japan. They express great respect for both the Panchen and Dalai Lamas. The monk said that he had visited China once forty years ago and that the sights he saw this time were very different from before. He also said that Buddhism was very prosperous in Latvia more than a thousand years ago, but it was destroyed by other religions, and the images and temples were gone. Now, after his best efforts, there is a gradual resurgence.

Hexiaojiao Villagers Appeal for Exemption from House Tax 145

There are more than 200 households in Hexiaojiao village in the Fahua district of western Shanghai, with a total population of more than 1,000 people. Most of them live in old-fashioned bungalows inherited from their ancestors. However, due to the Municipal Finance Bureau's collection of house tax, the farmers in the village were greatly alarmed. In May of last year, they requested that the decision be revoked, but the matter has not been resolved for a long time. Last month, the Finance Bureau suddenly ordered the police station to summon two farmers from the village to the station. As a result, four or five hundred farmers from the village gathered at the police station. Fortunately, the station chief's persuasion was effective. After the villagers returned to the village, they elected Wang Guangrun, Yang Xingchu, and two others as representatives. In addition to petitioning the municipal government, requesting that the Finance Bureau be instructed to exempt the village from house tax, the representatives are now carrying letters to various statutory organizations in the city, describing the current bankruptcy of rural areas and the difficult living conditions of the villagers, requesting that Mayor Wu be asked to consider the current situation and approve a postponement of the tax collection to maintain the livelihoods of the farmers.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Instructs Promissory Notes Should Have Stamps 146

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce replied to the Buffalo Hide and Straw Goods Trade Association, instructing that promissory notes should have stamps. On the 27th of this month, we received your letter asking whether promissory notes can also be exempted from stamps, as checks are exempted according to the fourth provision of the revised Stamp Tax Law rate schedule. After investigation, only the words "checks are temporarily exempted" appear in the tax exemption provision in the fourth provision of the revised Stamp Tax Law rate schedule promulgated by the National Government. Therefore, the stamp exemption is naturally limited to checks. Other bills of exchange, banknotes, and promissory notes are not exempt. The promissory notes issued by your industry should be stamped with two cents each in accordance with the law to avoid investigation and penalties. This is very important.

Economic Cooperative Society Promotes Business 148

The China Economic Credit Cooperative, founded by financial celebrities such as Zhang Shouyong, has been around for several years and is the first and largest credit cooperative in China. However, it was established at a time when the market was in decline. Nevertheless, those who joined the cooperative were still... Over the years, all industries in Shanghai have been struggling to make ends meet. The cooperative, based on the principle of cooperation and mutual assistance, and with fixed investment regulations, has been able to cope with the situation comfortably. Now, based on its years of experience and adopting the opinions of its members, the executive director Qiu Hanping has formulated a plan, which has been carefully revised by the chairman of the board, Zhang Shouyong, and has been submitted to the executive committee for approval. For the convenience of office work, the office will be moved to the third floor of the Women's Bank Building at 480 Nanjing Road starting on March 1. Now, details of the cooperative's recent situation are explored and described below, which should also be welcome to those who care about cooperative business.

Re-Registration The cooperative was established at a time when there was no Cooperative Law. Now the cooperative has been revised in accordance with the new law, and the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has issued a license numbered Xin Zi No. 1. The registered name is Shanghai China Economic Credit Insurance Limited Liability Cooperative.

Registered Business The cooperative, in accordance with Articles 3, Section 1, Clauses 4 and 5 of the Cooperative Law, operates (A) deposits and savings, (B) loans and discounts, (C) insurance for members' businesses, life, and disasters, and (D) mutual assistance businesses for members. All have been stated in the articles of association and approved for registration by the competent authorities.

Revised Measures Many members of the cooperative have complained that the previous methods of paying contributions in installments from the savings and life insurance fund were too long and cumbersome and have requested revisions. Now the cooperative has revised the contribution and guarantee procedures. Anyone who joins the cooperative and pays 35 yuan per month until December will have 1,000 yuan paid by the cooperative in one lump sum to the Bank of Communications for a 15-year term. The cooperative will also issue a life insurance payment order for 400 yuan. If a member dies prematurely, the payment will be made immediately. This method was pioneered by the cooperative, so that members and their families can benefit. If there is an urgent need in the middle, the order can be used as collateral for a loan without the need for a guarantor, which is very convenient.

The Economic Power of the British in Shanghai (Continued) 162

— Hu Yizang

Since the two major financial groups joined forces, silver prices unexpectedly fell, leading to inflation. At the same time, various countries were investing heavily in China. Taking advantage of this opportunity, they actively engaged in real estate, finance, and property development. Public utilities such as gas and water could even generate a net profit of more than 20%, propelling them to become the magnates they are today, wielding immense power.

Currently, Arnold serves as the Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Shanghai International Settlement, controlling the pivotal aspects of Shanghai's municipal administration. Victor Sassoon, the leader of the Sassoon financial group, advocated for a "Shanghai Pound System" last year as a countermeasure against China's currency instability. He is a British gentleman of Jewish descent, now in his sixties, and possesses remarkable insight into global affairs. Under the direct or indirect control of these two major financial groups, there are over twenty companies involved in banking, construction, trust, investment, gas, trade, maritime and land transportation, insurance, and other sectors. In particular, among the land and buildings, the so-called Sassoon House (the Cathay Hotel, Shanghai's only Hua Mao Hotel) and Hamilton House are both buildings owned by this financial group. Although the capital of the Sassoon Banking Corporation is only one million pounds, it also influences the major trends in Shanghai's exchange and gold markets. It is estimated that the total investment of these two financial groups in Shanghai is around 150 to 160 million yuan. Since the rise of the movement for the restoration of national rights in China, the custody of tariff revenue was transferred from HSBC to the Central Bank due to tariff autonomy. Recently, due to the global economic downturn, drastic fluctuations in silver prices, the decline in the purchasing power of the Chinese people in the interior, and the overall expansion and leap of Japan's political economy, the economic power of the British has been significantly threatened. In other words, Japan's political and economic activity and Britain's China policy are fundamentally in conflict. For example, in Manchuria and Shanghai, Manchuria has gained the support of Japan and will extend from North China to South China. Shanghai is under pressure from Japanese forces. As a result, the original British power is gradually declining. Judging from the recent trade situation between Japan and Britain, Japan has surpassed Britain. The expansion of Japanese power can be clearly understood by comparing the trade between Shanghai and Japan and Britain in the past year and the year before. (To be continued)

"North China Daily News" Cup Replay: You You Eliminates Tung Wah 165

Tung Wah Takes the Early Lead, First Half Ends in a Draw

Overall Result: You You Wins 7-2 to Advance to the Semifinals

The "North China Daily News" Cup soccer tournament has been underway for some time and has reached the semi-final stage. However, the match between Tung Wah B and You You B ended in a 1-1 draw last week and a replay was held yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM at the Shen Yuan Stadium. Both sides fielded crack troops and the battle was evenly matched. In the first half, Tung Wah took the early lead, and then the You You players strive to attack, making a 2-2 draw. In the second half, Tung Wah's defense was slightly lax, and the You You forwards took advantage of this to score five goals in a row. Although Tung Wah tried hard to break through, the time was running out, and the bell rang to end the game. The final score was 7-2, with You You eliminating Tung Wah to advance to the semi-finals. The lineups of both sides are as follows:

You You B

Tung Wah B

The Tung Wah team opened the scoring. It was time, the referee He Chunhui, Hu Jiasheng stood up and began to engage in contact, Tung Wah took the offensive first, Chen Dehui offered his magic weapon, Wang Zhangbao intercepted halfway, Dehui made a comeback, Cao Qinfang took the grass to transport grain, forward and backward, and went to a considerable area, Dehui did not fail his mission, and shot with his feet at the ten-yard mark, straight into the core, opening the scoring, You You lost, and the whole army was furious. Qiaosheng raised the banner at the border, sneaking around, and a shot at the door, Dang'an was quick-eyed and quick-handed, waving his fists to strike it out, Qiaosheng hurried to catch up, and returned without success, Qiaosheng was familiar with the road, and re-entered, the shot was blocked, Xue Yongyuan the fisherman benefited, and kicked it in calmly, creating a draw, Tung Wah Cao Qinfang refused to show weakness, and went deep into the tiger's den alone, Zhu Qiu lost his footing in front of the horse, Cao Qinfang would not let the opportunity pass, and returned to the division, at this time You You was not discouraged, and calmly fought, Qiaosheng built a road across the border, and passed the ball to the middle army, Hui Peiren had long legs and was fast, and kicked it into the corner, not long after, the horn sounded, and the two sides drew 2-2, ending the first half.

You You won 7-2. Switching sides and fighting again, You You's arrogance was very high. Xu Wenkui passed the barrier and cut the general, unstoppable. Xi Qiaosheng helped the tyrant to abuse, and the road was as smooth as a knife, approaching Tung Wah's inland, cleverly shooting at the fifteen-yard mark, Guan Dang'an was caught off guard for a while, and the position was immediately lost. Regulations on Rewards and Punishments for Personnel Engaged in Compulsory Literacy Education 183

Filed with the Ministry of Education for Approval

The Ministry of Education previously approved the Jiangsu Provincial Government's request to formulate and promulgate regulations for promoting compulsory literacy education in the province, and requested that they be filed with the Ministry. The Provincial Government believes that the lack of universal literacy education is a major obstacle to the implementation of government policies and a hidden worry for the nation. It is determined to achieve practical results, but at this time of frequent disasters and difficulties for both the public and private sectors, there is a lack of adequate special funds and facilities. Therefore, it relies on the efforts of officials and people throughout the province to raise funds. Fortunately, the Baojia system has been used to establish a preliminary framework. By promoting it in this way, it will be of great benefit to eliminating illiteracy in the province. The Provincial Government previously stipulated that those counties that complete the initial literacy education work on schedule would be included as one of the performance evaluations of the county heads and directors, and ordered that this be implemented. Now, in order to facilitate assessment, in accordance with Article 17 of the Provincial Government's previous "Preliminary Measures for the Implementation of Compulsory Education in Various Counties," the "Jiangsu Provincial Regulations on Rewards and Punishments for Personnel Engaged in Compulsory Literacy Education in Various Counties" has been formulated to promote progress. Please consider filing them for record, which is very convenient, etc. The reply stated that the formulated regulations on rewards and punishments have been reviewed and are in compliance, and should be filed for record as requested. The 16 articles of the regulations on rewards and punishments for personnel engaged in compulsory literacy education in various counties formulated by the province stipulate that county heads, directors of education bureaus, directors of public security bureaus, district chiefs, township chiefs, Bao chiefs, personnel in charge of public security affairs, heads of social education institutions, and school principals who are able to complete the preliminary plan in the 25th year of the Republic, raise funds effectively, be able to economize on expenditures, work diligently, and effectively supervise the attendance rate of enrolled people in the county to average 85% or more per month, and the graduation rate of students in the county to be 85% or more of enrolled people will be rewarded separately. Those who fail to hold the event without reason, perform poorly, achieve no results, or whose attendance rate of enrolled people averages 40% or less per month, and whose graduation rate of students in the county is 40% or less will be punished separately.

Xiangya Medical College Has Already Improved According to Orders 184

The Hunan Xiangya Medical College, previously received instructions from the Ministry of Education to diligently implement and report on improvements based on the key points of the inspection report. "According to the key points provided, the improvement report includes: ㈠ The annual budget of the college consists of three items: subsidies from the Hunan Provincial Government, subsidies from the American Yale-China Association, and income from the hospital. Equipment expenses are subsidized by the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board of Trustees and the Ministry. The total annual income is more than 200,000 yuan, but the subsidies from the provincial government are heavily in arrears, causing some difficulties. The school medical committee has been asked to plan a fund to handle this effectively. ㈡ 'Adding teaching staff to the basic faculty': Starting this academic year, new teachers have been added, such as Dr. Bai Shien from Peking Union Medical College for bacteriology, Lao Qixiang for mathematics, He Jiasheng for physical education, Chen Renlie for physics, and Ling Xiaoying for embryology. Each department has dedicated personnel responsible for teaching. ㈢ 'Increased equipment': The main instruments for each laboratory have been added, including a magic lantern, 36 microscopes, a generator, and over a hundred types of books and magazines. Others are being purchased and will soon arrive in Hunan. A library has also been established, accommodating over a hundred people for reading. ㈣ 'Improved teaching': The college has been teaching in English since the eighteenth year. Since its opening, the college has advocated using Mandarin Chinese, but due to difficulties such as the lack of standardized terminology and suitable Mandarin medical textbooks, it has not been fully implemented. Currently, Mandarin is mostly used for teaching in lower grades to reduce students' difficulties, while upper grades should be given the convenience of reading Western reference books, so English must be used. Senior students can fully understand English. In the future, when the terminology is finalized and more domestic medical books are published, Mandarin Chinese can be used for all teaching." The above four items truthfully state the situation and are submitted for review and approval. The Ministry of Education has instructed that the reported improvements are generally acceptable and should be implemented diligently.

Tai Shuangqiu's Popular Education Vehicle Invention Will Be Publicly Demonstrated in Shanghai on a Fixed Date 187

And Host Reporters from Local Newspapers

To Report on the Invention Process and Scope of Application

Dr. Tai Shuangqiu, Dean of the School of Education at Great China University, previously felt that the Western-style school education was not suitable for China today. He spent three years inventing the Popular Education Vehicle. The Ministry of Education reviewed it and deemed it a useful tool for promoting popular education, ordering it to be adopted nationwide. Mr. Tai has scheduled a public demonstration for the Shanghai press community on March 10th to explore the invention process and scope of application, etc. as follows:

Invention Process 188

In the autumn of 1933, Mr. Tai felt that the Western-style school education system was not suitable for China's needs today. Based on his research findings, he created a Popular Education Vehicle. Its form is a rectangular wooden box with very simple contents. After more than a dozen improvements, it was tested in the Shanghai Civil Education Experimental Zone jointly established by the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, Great China University, and the Popular Education Movement Promotion Association for as long as two years before it was completed.

Structure and Content 189

The Popular Education Vehicle has the appearance of a square wooden box with three wheels at the bottom. The painted boards on the front and back of the vehicle can be used as blackboards or transformed into long tables for various activities such as displaying exhibitions and playing table tennis. There is an iron frame on top, which is usually placed inside the vehicle and taken out when needed to build a shed for hanging blackboards, charts, oil lamps, paintings, abacuses, etc. A cloth curtain can also be stretched on top. The vehicle frame and edges have rulers for measuring height and cloth. The vehicle contains five sets of movable popular education items. The box shells can be opened to serve as blackboards. The box is divided into storage for hygiene, teaching, entertainment, crafts, and agricultural exhibition supplies, which can be taken as needed. The box can be carried on the back over mountains and waters, reaching far and wide. The vehicle also has four folding educational stools, which take up very little space and can provide seating for eight people when unfolded. They are sturdy and safe from tipping.

Scope of Application 190

The application of the Popular Education Vehicle is extensive, roughly including the following: ㈠ County education bureaus and education sections can purchase the vehicle to promote free education, especially the mobile education stipulated in the outline of free education implementation measures, which cannot be promoted without using the vehicle. ㈡ Local mass education centers, farmer education centers, libraries, etc. can use the vehicle to create mobile education centers or mobile libraries to promote mass education outside the centers. ㈢ Local people's schools can purchase the vehicle to create mobile people's schools to increase the efficiency of people's education. ㈣ Local primary and secondary schools can use the vehicle for public education and people's education to train students' ability to serve the community. ㈤ Local education departments should use the vehicle as the central hub to guide and assist in the popularization of education. ㈥ University education departments, normal colleges, local normal schools, and normal departments of middle schools should offer "mobile education" courses using the vehicle for students. ㈦ Other educational organizations and groups should use the vehicle to assist in free education.

Public Demonstration 191

The vehicle has twelve functions: mobile library, traveling teaching platform, mass newspaper, mobile exhibition, alternative venue, civilian desk, temporary hospital, cooperative store, simple factory, agricultural guidance, entertainment venue, and open-air tea garden. One person can manage this vehicle and travel around the countryside. Mr. Tai has scheduled a reception for the local press community at 6:30 PM on March 2nd at the Yizhi Xiang Vegetarian Restaurant on Simalu and will give a public demonstration.
