Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (1)(8)(6) 195

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Chapter X Gratitude

This annual Thanksgiving Day at Plumfield was celebrated in the old good way, without interruption. For several days before, the little girls had been assisting Aunt Jo and Mrs. Bhaer in the pantry and kitchen making various pastries, selecting fruit pulp, and scrubbing dishes, all of which were very busy and self-important. The boys lingered on the border of that forbidden land, smelling the fragrant smells, peering into those secret workshops, or tasting a little of the delicacies still in the making.

This year there seemed to be something going on that was not in previous years, because the children were rattling up and down the stairs, and the boys were also busy in the classroom and warehouse. They were dumping baskets and boxes, searching for old ribbons and lace and other delicate fabrics, and a large number of grass blades, cotton, flannel, as well as large black beads, for Frau Bhaer and Mrs. Jo. Nat was busily working away at those strange machines in the factory, and Little Jo and Tommy each kept muttering to themselves as if trying to memorize something, sometimes audible with a terrifying sound emitted by Emil. And sometimes when Mrs. Bhaer et al wanted Rob and Teddy to go, they were not seen for several hours, we heard bursts of laughter from the nursery. But what puzzled Mr. Bhaer most was where Rob's big pumpkin had gone. It was indeed happily sent into the kitchen, and soon appeared a dozen butterscotch pie. But this does not eliminate a quarter of the giant melon, where is the rest? It was always a mystery, Rob seems not care, laughing when someone talked about it, asked his father to "wait and see", because the whole thing was to surprise Uncle Bhaer in the end, do not let him know a little bit in advance.

Finance: The Gold Market Is Unstable, with Nervous Sentiment... The Result Is Flat 196

The gold market was erratic yesterday, with fluctuating sentiment. It weakened slightly due to large-scale selling, but Japanese news remained serious, and buying interest was strong, briefly breaking through the 50 yuan level. Early in the morning, overseas silver markets showed British narrowing and American leveling. Floor traders said that the market would weaken after closing. There were buyers at the listed price, but sellers also at 0.0625 lower. Deferred silver prices on the Comex fell more than they rose. Exchange rates were flat. London spot gold rose half a penny. Over-the-counter forward trading opened around 49.5 yuan. Dadecheng, Yicheng, and Dingkang sold to within 9 yuan. The Central Bank announced listed rates, with British and American rates unchanged. Customs gold units remained unchanged. The listed price for standard gold was raised to 1147.3 yuan and then hovered. The morning opened lower. Sentiment was still good after opening, approaching the 50 yuan level. Banks took the opportunity to sell off, and large investors came to force sales, urgently going downstream. However, there was some support after falling. Although the HSBC listed rate was flat, it had little impact. Later, the silver equalization tax was announced as unchanged. Buying interest in the market revived, gradually approaching the 50 yuan level. There were also many who took the opportunity to sell at high prices, and the situation was fluctuating again. Later, rumors spread that the situation in Japan was increasingly terrifying, with residents fleeing to avoid danger. Sentiment suddenly rose, and Japanese banks no longer absorbed Eastbound remittances, thus breaking through the 50 yuan level. However, the afternoon closing still succumbed to below 50 yuan. Reading Club

From Ming Dynasty Literature to the Public Security Jingling School 217

— Pei Wei

From the Yongle period of the Ming Dynasty to the early Hongzhi period, because it experienced a relatively long period of peace and stability, and the rural economy was stable, and the political system was on track, the literary style of the imperial court was at its peak, and the cabinet style of the Three Yangs represented this era. After the Hongzhi and Zhengde periods, the northwest was afflicted by bandits, and eunuchs monopolized the government. The era of peace was over. Generally people gradually became disgusted with the literary style of the imperial court. There was the retro movement of the former and later Seven Masters. The revivalists imitated the Qin and Han dynasties to make fake ancient texts, and talked about the great principles of governing the country and bringing peace to the world. This was because the situation had not yet reached an irreversible point, so they could still put on airs and talk nonsense. Later, as politics became worse and worse, and the rural economy was on the verge of bankruptcy, the literati were dissatisfied with the current political situation, and they could not think of a way to remedy it for a while. Simply, they did not put on airs in their articles, and did not talk about the great principles of governing the country and bringing peace to the world. Therefore, the Public Security School, which advocated "expressing one's spirit and not sticking to fixed patterns," and the Jingling School, which intentionally made articles difficult for people to understand, arose one after another. However, from the Tianqi period to the fall of the Ming Dynasty, the stimuli suffered by the literati were too deep, and many people opposed "independent spirit" and began to produce passionate and tragic works. After the Southern Capital, there were more poems about frost and chaos, and articles about millet and wheat, full of sadness and sorrow, which were completely different from those so-called "fresh, light, and graceful" or "dark, deep, and lonely." In the early Qing Dynasty, Zhang Dai (Zongzi), who claimed to be the culmination of the Public Security and Jingling schools, had a different content, structure, and style in his articles from the Public Security and Jingling schools. We only need to compare his works with the works of the Three Yuan and Zhong Tan, and we will know.

Looking at the evolution of literature in the Ming Dynasty, the Public Security Jingling schools were just a temporary reaction to the Revivalists. Their rise, growth, and decline were very short-lived, and their influence was not very great. Recently, the names of the Public Security Jingling schools have been mentioned more and more often, and the collections of poems and essays by the Three Yuan and Zhong Tan are popular in the market again. Literary historians also have to talk about the Public Security Jingling schools in detail when they talk about Ming Dynasty literature, so as not to be criticized. The fact that the Three Yuan and Zhong Tan suddenly got such good luck three hundred years later is really unexpected. However, in such an era and such a country, should this school of literature be promoted?

Choosing Children's Books 218

— Wei Zhi

When choosing children's books, we need to set some standards. If there are no standards, "anything in the basket is food." Just giving children some reading material may not necessarily be good for them. It may be worse than not giving them anything at all.

First, the meaning must be proper. This does not mean that things like birds and animal stories cannot be read to them. Birds and animal stories are just a matter of form. What we need to pay special attention to is the content of the reading material. Whenever a piece of writing is written, whether good or bad, it must have the author's central content, which we call meaning. If the meaning is proper, then it is okay to read it even if it uses the form of bird and animal stories. Otherwise, it is not readable even if it is completely human language. Where do we distinguish between proper and improper? Just think: the readers are Chinese children, modern Chinese children, and what meets the needs of modern Chinese children is proper. Conversely, it is improper. For example: what is in accordance with the principles of physics is proper, and what contains superstitious ideas is abnormal. What promotes the spirit of collectivism is proper, and what promotes the legacy of feudalism is abnormal. —— By analogy, we can give many examples, so there is no need to elaborate here.

Second, the writing must be coherent. This standard is a bit strange. If it is written as children's reading material and printed on paper, can the writing still be incoherent? Ideally, there should be none. However, the children's reading materials that are currently popular, whether they are compiled or translated, often have unclear, disjointed, stiff, and difficult-to-read sentences. Generally, these problems are included in incoherence. Since there are indeed incoherent children's reading materials, we must pay attention when choosing them and exclude them. Children are cultivating their language habits while reading children's books. If this kind of incoherent writing is used as a model of language, it will make them unable to speak well, and gradually make them unable to turn a thought in an orderly manner. This influence is not slight.

Third, if it is poetry, it must be like poetry. Flattery and glibness are not poetry. Casual rhyme is not poetry. If there are pictures, they must be like a picture. What does not look like anything is certainly not a picture. If it looks like something but is stiff and lifeless, it cannot be considered a picture. Giving children things that do not look like anything is enough to inhibit their interest in that kind of thing, which is really a kind of abuse. Poetry and pictures are most loved by children, and are most helpful for children's enlightenment. Therefore, special attention must be paid when choosing, to reject those that do not look like anything and leave those that look like something.

"Twenty-Five Histories Supplement Compilation" General Rules 219

This compilation is limited to tables and treatises. All works of addition, annotation, textual research, and collation, whether they are the lost works of ancient sages or recent works of contemporary scholars, are included as far as knowledge extends. This is because learning values breadth and comprehensiveness, not narrow specialization; the duty lies in extensive collection, without shying away from promotion.

All tables and treatises with clear headings and distinct systems, whether published separately, in collections, or as appendices to books, such as the "Han Shu Yi Wen Zhi Kao Zheng" appended to "Yu Hai," the "Han Zhi Zhi Yi" appended to "Shui Jing Zhu Tu," and the "Liao Yi Wen Zhi" appended to "Liao Wen Cun," are all included. Those that are attached to complete works and difficult to separate, such as the works of Shen Qinhan, Zhou Shouchang, and Wang Xianqian on the "Han Shu," although they each have a table of contents, are actually part of a separate book and difficult to divide, so they are omitted.

The entire book is arranged according to the order of the dynastic histories, divided into sections. Each section begins with tables and then treatises, grouped by category. The recording of books also briefly explains the author's era to create order. Those that specifically describe the political systems and reforms of partial regimes and the activities of foreign tribes are placed at the end of each section to clarify the organization, such as Lian Shu's "Western Qin Hundred Officials Table" and Shen Weixian's "Two Han Xiongnu Table" and "Jin Dynasty Five Hu Table."

Since the arrangement of this compilation is based on the complete system of each dynastic history, the division of sections should be clear and not intertwined. Except for Xu Wenfan's "Eastern Jin Southern and Northern Dynasties Geography Table" and Qian Daxin's "Liao Jin Yuan History Leap Month Examination," which cannot be cut, we will allocate them according to their tendency. Other works, such as Wan Sitong's "Historical Tables of Past Dynasties" and Xie Zhongying's "Three Kingdoms Major Events Table," are all assigned to their respective categories without mixing them. The original catalog of the main source or earlier publication is recorded to preserve the original state. Brief explanations are added to indicate the reasons for changes.

Among the books collected, those that completely record the original text of the old histories but separately discuss or collate them, such as the "Du Shi Ji Shi Biao" with annotations, are treated like Xia Xie's "Jiao Han Shu Ba Biao," only including the summary and removing the old text. This is because the complete "Twenty-Five Histories" is already available, so there is no need to repeat it, which would only take up space.

At the beginning of this compilation, except for a small part of the manuscripts that are heavily marked and cannot be photocopied, the rest are intended to be reduced and printed using photographic zinc plates. However, upon careful examination of each book, some woodblock prints are blurred and unclear, such as Zhang Zongyuan's "Sui Shu Jing Ji Zhi Kao Zheng" and Lü Wutiaoyang's "Han Shu Di Li Zhi Xiang Shi"; some collations are not precise, and there are errors to be corrected, such as Bao's engraved "Wu Zhuoxin's Han Shu Di Li Zhi Bu Zhu" (the so-called excellent versions of Wang Yuansun, Qian Dian, and Quan Zuwang's Han Zhi also have occasional misprints); some have complex formats and small fonts that do not meet the compilation's reduction standards, such as the Guangya version of "Eastern Jin Southern and Northern Dynasties Geography Table"; some are originally letterpress or lithograph and cannot be reduced and reproduced, such as Gu San's "Bu Hou Han Shu Yi Wen Zhi" and Ding Xitian's "Hou Han Jun Guo Ling Zhang Kao Bu"; and some have paper that is too old and dark to be photographed. Since there are no other versions to replace them, we cannot allow the errors to persist, which would be regrettable, so we have decided to uniformly use typesetting. The original large characters are in size five, and the small characters are in size six. All are vertical, without interlinear notes. The typesetting is very clear, and the lines are uniform. Any obvious errors or omissions in the citations can be corrected at any time based on the original text.

Regarding the choice of versions: for those with many copies, the first edition is taken. If there are differences in the engraved versions or the number of volumes varies, the best or complete version is taken. For works supplemented by later scholars, which include the original authors' works when published, such as Xie Zhongying's work on Hong Liangji and Yang Shoujing's work on Wu Zeng, the later version is taken directly, still bearing the original author's name, so that the length is saved, and the origin is not obscured. If there are obvious differences between the published version and the manuscript, the two versions are collated without hesitation to reproduce them, such as Wan Sitong's "Southern Tang Generals and Ministers Chronological Table" and other six types.

Tables are used horizontally and diagonally, which is beneficial for clear latitude and longitude and easy communication. However, there are also those that have the same nature but different formats, those that have no fixed standards for dividing items, those that divide and transfer lines due to too many horizontal bars, which confuse the system, and those that fill in grids without any vertical or horizontal relationship. The spacing is wide, wasting paper. Therefore, for genealogical tables with horizontal and vertical relationships, such as Zhou Mingtai's "Three Kingdoms Genealogy Table," and official position tables and geography tables with division and combination relationships, such as Hong Yisun's "Three Kingdoms Zhi Official Position Table" and Wu Zeng's "Three Kingdoms Prefecture and County Table," the original format is still used. For other major events tables, official position tables, and generation tables mainly based on the inheritance of titles that have no vertical and horizontal division and combination relationships, they are all changed to vertical writing, following the example of Dun Xiong's "Hou Han Shu Chronological Table Collation and Supplement." For horizontal branching text, the traces of front and back connections must be noted to ensure that the system is not chaotic and the latitude and longitude are still very clear. Readers should understand this humble intention.

The main purpose of collation is to seek truth. If there are any uncertainties, comparisons must be made. For variant characters and divergent meanings, the best is chosen, and those that must be explained are also attached to the book as collation notes or postscripts to show caution. However, the knowledge and ability of colleagues are limited, and there must be many mistakes. How dare we try to embellish our work? We hope that knowledgeable people will not hesitate to teach us so that we can correct them during the printing process. It would be fortunate for scholarship and fortunate for our colleagues.

Two Collections of Short Stories 220

— Ba Jin

— Postscript to Ba Jin's Collection of Short Stories —

It has been several years since I started writing. I sometimes cannot figure out what I have written in these years. Thinking about it, some of my articles were discarded as soon as they were written, and some disappeared after they were published without my noticing. The few novels that have been circulated to this day.

The word "circulated" here makes me feel embarrassed. Just because they are "circulated" does not mean they are good things. Although today's fashionable bookstore owners can talk about "cultural standpoints" and print books in multiple editions, even four or five editions. So the fact that my books can be circulated to this day is not a glorious thing.

I am not satisfied with my own works. I cherish them sometimes, but I also hate them sometimes. And one thing remains constant: every time I read what I have written, I cannot help but pick up a pen and make random deletions and revisions. It seems that there are flaws everywhere, and I cannot feel comfortable unless I change them. According to a third-rate English critic, a good article cannot be deleted or revised at will. Not even a single word can be added or removed. From this, it can be seen that my articles are worthless.

Although that is what I say, I still do not have the courage to destroy my worthless articles, so I let them be printed in multiple editions in a muddled way. I do not want to make money, but I have never used culture as a front. My life is full of contradictions. For example, I am not satisfied with my own articles, but at the same time, I am unwilling to see those even more worthless books being sold to readers all the time. So I am happy to let my works compete with them for business.

I used to be busy writing articles. In the past year, I have invented (?) the word "laying down my pen" to perfunctorily deal with the great editors, so I have time to read. Sometimes I also read what I have written and spent some effort to organize my old works. As a result, I compiled two collections of short stories, including all of my short stories. I also attached a review of my writing life at the beginning, which is an old work, but with new material added. If readers cannot understand my novels, then the review of my writing life can help them. But if they still cannot understand after reading it, then they should simply not read it anymore or advise others not to read it. This is the most enjoyable way.

Editor's Note: The second collection of Ba Jin's short stories is currently being printed and will soon be published by Kaiming Bookstore.

"Science" Magazine's Criticism of "Biographical Sketches of Biology" 221

Although there are many publications in the book market in recent years, most of them are humorous essays or reprints of ancient books. In our opinion, in this era of famine for scientific knowledge, publications that benefit young students in general are in fact even leading ambitious young people to become passive or degenerate due to being drugged enough. On the other hand, many science books are also published by various bookstores, some of which are of course too specialized for the average person to understand; some are school textbooks that do not suit the taste of the average person. There are too few works that can both describe scientific facts and have literary meaning. The author of this book is known for writing science essays well. The book contains twenty-one biology essays, named "Biographical Sketches of Biology," which uses literary brushstrokes to describe scientific theories, so that readers can have literary appreciation and at the same time gain scientific knowledge, lightly sketched, from shallow to deep, full of interest. Sometimes, it quotes ancient poems, so that readers do not feel bored and can be nurtured by literature. Each article also has illustrations, which can increase scientific aesthetics. Young people who are generally bored can certainly regard it as a proper pastime, get considerable benefits, and increase a lot of common sense. From the perspective of popularizing scientific knowledge, this is also the best way to get started. From a scientific standpoint, what the reading community in our country needs now is not so much "humor" and "chat," but science works that are both literary and rational, which are pleasant and beneficial. We are extremely in favor of Mr. Jia's book being published and hope that it will greatly open up the atmosphere and renew the trend in the reading community. At the same time, we also hope that other scholars who are proficient in both literature and science in astronomy, physics, chemistry, and geography can make the same contributions in their spare time. The book's format, printing, and paper are all good. The actual price of four corners seems a little expensive. (Published in Science, Volume 20, Issue 2, pages 152, 153)

A Report on Soliciting Readers' Opinions on the Inaugural Issue of "New Youth" 222

— Editor

After the inaugural issue of "New Youth" was published, it was warmly welcomed by readers. The number of copies printed increased from 50,000 to 80,000, and from 80,000 to 100,000, but it was still not enough to distribute, which we had not expected at the beginning. We are naturally only redoubling our efforts to thank the 100,000 readers who love us for this extraordinary honor. However, we know that our abilities are weak and our knowledge is incomplete. There must still be many things that should be supplemented or improved in what we have contributed to "New Youth." Therefore, we published a brief announcement in the second issue of the "Reading Club" on January 16, stipulating two topics: (1) Reading the inaugural issue of "New Youth," and (2) What I hope from "New Youth," to solicit guidance and criticism from readers as a compass for future editing. As of February 10, we actually received fourteen solicited articles. Among them, eight articles were written using the first topic, and the content of each article was more about encouragement and less about guidance. Six articles were written using the second topic, and each article put forward several opinions and requirements.

Now, let's organize these articles, summarize them, and report them below:

1. Hope to distribute the amount of "literature," "social science," and "natural science" evenly.

2. Hope to publish more research methods for various disciplines.

3. Hope to add more detailed analysis and research to the current situation.

4. Instill the essentials of "national salvation and survival" and patriotic propositions.

5. Hope to publish some texts about occupations.

6. Publish more current affairs photos, cartoons, and illustrations.

7. Pay attention to the needs of all teenagers (living in various different environments).

8. Do your best to introduce or create the most valuable and cutting-edge knowledge in all disciplines.

9. Focus on practical things as materials, and be willing to cut off irrelevant high-level discussions.

10. Pay attention to the popularization of texts.

11. Young texts should strive for novelty and interest.

12. Please set up a question and answer column for teenagers to answer all the difficult questions of readers.

13. Receive submissions and often solicit articles as much as possible to encourage and guide readers to write.

14. I hope that all of them will be typeset in size five, which can increase some pages.

15. It is best to change to weekly or semi-monthly, so that you do not meet after half a month.

16. Hope to have more experts in various disciplines write.

17. Hope to maintain the splendor of the inaugural issue and strive for excellence.

Here, let us divide the seventeen points indicated by readers into three categories to give readers a brief reply:

The first category is what we have already implemented, such as points (1), (3), (4), (6), (8), (9), (10), (11), (14), (16), and (17). Readers only need to look at issues 2, 3, and 4 of this magazine to understand. The second category is what we are planning, such as points (2), (5), (7), and (13). The third category is what we feel we cannot implement for a while, that is, only points (12) and (15). The inability to implement these two points is entirely a matter of manpower. (12) is the hope that we will set up a question and answer column. According to our past experience, we feel that once there is a question and answer column in the magazine, there will be a lot of letters asking questions. As a result, only one-tenth or two-tenths can be published; it is of course not possible to answer them one by one due to the number of pages and manpower, but we feel that it is a bit unreasonable to ask but not answer, which would cost readers a few cents for postage. (15) is the hope to change it to weekly or semi-monthly. This is also a matter of manpower, and the number of pages for weekly or semi-monthly publications cannot be too many, because if there are more pages, it will invisibly increase the burden on readers. If the number of pages is reduced, it is difficult to say whether it can still maintain its original appearance.

Soliciting Criticism on Semi-Monthly New Books 223

Since September of last year, this bookstore has launched the "Semi-Monthly New Books" and "Special Price 30% off" method, which has been six months now; there are a total of fifty books published. This method is convenient for readers, and we would like to know which books most readers like and what their feelings are after reading them. Please give us guidance and criticism in many ways as much as possible! We welcome submissions, whether long or short, and will publish them in this publication successively. Sincerely, Kaiming Bookstore

Shen Bao Children's Supplement

Shen Bao Children's Volunteer Essay

What Kind of Person Will I Be in the Future 224

— Huang Yafang, Mingcheng Elementary School, Haimen County, Jiangsu Province

"What kind of person will I be in the future?" This is indeed a very important question. In the past few days, I spent several days to answer it before I came up with a final answer. Although I am a female elementary school student, I don't have any ambitions or responsibilities now, but what about the future? I am always a member of the country, and I must at least be a good wife and mother to my family, and of course, I must do my best to my country; in this way, I cannot have no goals in life because I am young. Modern women cannot be compared with ancient women. In ancient times, being a good wife and mother was considered a lifetime of responsibility, as if it had nothing to do with the country and society. Now, in addition to the family, women also have to bear part of the duty of saving the country. Our China is so weak, although men should use all their energy to save the country, how can we women forget the work of saving the country? For example, once our country goes to war with the enemy, men go to the front line, and the rear work is the duty of us women. Sometimes the front line needs nurses for rescue, and we have to rush to the front line to serve. I often hear teachers say: "Women only work at home in peacetime, and they have to go to the front line like men in wartime." Ah! Should we be such a modern woman? I also think: a good wife and mother is not just about treating her husband and children well. We must make a family harmonious and able to work hard and be frugal, and create a happy family. Only then can individuals have happiness, and only when every family can do well can society and the country have hope. The above words are my goals in life in the future.

Alarm Pillow 225

— Xu Xiaoting

There are things in society that are used to warn people, such as alarm clocks and sirens. Now we have found another fact about alarm pillows from old books, and we are writing it down below:

Sima Wengong of the Song Dynasty was a famous Confucian scholar of the Zhu Dynasty. During his studies, he was deeply worried that his studies would not succeed. He usually lived in seclusion and studied hard. He specially made a round wooden pillow, with his head on it. If he moved a little, the pillow would roll. Even when he was in a deep sleep, he would be awakened. Therefore, he was called the alarm pillow. When he was tired of reading, he would fall asleep, but he would use a round pillow to warn him. After waking up, he would study again. He did this every day, reading tirelessly. Later, he became a great Confucian scholar. It was not easy for him to enjoy a great reputation in later generations!

Children all over the country! You are all mostly in the stage of studying now. During this most difficult period of the country, "reading does not forget to save the country, and saving the country does not forget to read," you must be moved by the facts of Sima Wengong's alarm pillow. I hope you will rise up with enthusiasm, study hard from now on, and cultivate useful talents so that you can contribute to the country in the future.

Solidification and Melting 227

— Zhen

Playing with snowballs is Min'er's favorite game in winter. So when it snows, he goes to school very early. But he hates the melting snow the most. The ground is difficult to walk, and the weather is very cold. He feels very strange, so he went home after school and asked his father:

"Dad, do you know why it is much colder when the snow melts than when it is snowing?"

"Do you want to know why it is cold when the snow melts? Then you must first know whether the weather is cold or not when the snow solidifies? I said that the snow is not much colder when it solidifies than when the snow melts, because when a liquid solidifies into a solid, it must release heat. What is the reason for this?"

So his father took a glass tube and a cup, put half of the water in the glass tube, and put some ice and salt in the cup. He put the glass tube in the middle of the ice and salt, and took a thermometer, first put it in the glass tube, and saw that the temperature of the water dropped to zero degrees, and the water gradually solidified into ice. His father opened his mouth and said:

"The temperature when the water solidifies stays at zero degrees and will not change until the water completely solidifies into ice. The temperature of the ice only begins to drop again. From this, it can be seen that the water will not drop to zero degrees when it solidifies, because it is releasing heat."

"As for melting, how can it be cold? When the snow melts, it must absorb heat to melt. You just need to take the cup you just took, put ice in it, heat it, and measure its temperature with a thermometer. The temperature of the snow, initially heated, reaches zero degrees and no longer rises until the snow completely melts into water, and the temperature of the water gradually rises. You can try it yourself."

"Dad, how much heat does it take for a solid to melt into a liquid?"

"This question is very complicated. Let me tell you a little bit. One gram of ice, when it melts into zero-degree water at zero degrees, must absorb 80 calories of heat. What is called a calorie? The heat required for one gram of water to increase one degree in temperature is used as a unit of heat measurement, which is called a calorie."

Five Minute Fairytales 229

— Ren

Monkey Show

In the open space, many children gathered in a circle, watching the monkey show. The monkey sometimes wears a golden crown, playing the role of an ancient emperor. Sometimes, he wears a command knife with a clanging sound, playing the role of a modern general; because he plays the show too seriously, he even forgets that he is a monkey. When he was playing the emperor, he saw a beautiful girl in the crowd, and he ran up to her, about to hug her, and shouted "My empress..." when the monkey player pulled the rope around his neck and pulled him back to the center of the field to continue the show, so he had to obediently follow the rope.

When he was playing the general, he saw a dirty boy in the crowd, making faces and mocking him, and he ran up to him, about to raise the command knife, wanting to chop him, when the monkey player pulled the rope around his neck and pulled him back to the center of the field to continue the show, so he had to obediently follow the rope.

"Chop... clap... chop... clap..." The children threw copper coins to the monkey player's feet, and they clapped and cheered, saying: "This monkey show is well done!"

The monkey player collected the money and put it in his pocket. He took the monkey to a small restaurant, where he ate and drank until he was drunk and full, but he gave the monkey a little leftover soup to fill his hunger.

Firecrackers Ring All Over the World

A firecracker said to many children: "Don't be afraid of me. You should send me to the sky. Some firecrackers, once they go to the sky, their stomachs are broken, their bodies are shattered, and they make a bang, scaring your guts to pieces and deafening your ears. They are really harmful! I will never be like them. Once I go to the sky, I will never change my stomach, not explode my body, not make scary noises, and not release annoying gunpowder gas. I want to give you peace! Quiet. Hurry up and send me to the sky!"

The children believed her words and lit her gunpowder fuse. The firecracker got fire, look, it窜into the high sky. Wow! How proud he is!

But, you hear: "Bang... bang... clap... clap...!" So loud. Gunpowder gas filled the air, and unrest filled the ground. The children were all scared pale, some hiding, some escaping...

Originally, this firecracker only asked the children to send him to the sky, and the words he promised them at first were just to deceive them.

Happy Childhood Life 230

— Written by Zhang Chongren

A Small Study on Tails 231

— Yi'an

Many animals have tails. Although human tails are no longer visible, it is said that humans also had tails in primitive times. This theory is based on the structure at the end of our spine, and even now some people still have short tails, but the number is extremely small.

Apart from humans, almost all vertebrates have tails. If we observe their skeletons, we can see a series of bone segments, long or short, at the end of their spines, which are easily bent. The closer to the end, the smaller the bone segments, and this is their tail.

The size of the tail varies depending on how a particular animal uses its tail. Most bears have short tails, and the hippopotamus's tail is also disproportionate to its massive body. But some animals have tails that are two or three times longer than their bodies.

In summer, if we carefully observe a cow and see flies bothering it, we can appreciate one of the functions of the tail. At the end of its tail, there is a cluster of slender hairs, which is a tool that makes it more effective in driving away flies.

Some monkeys use their tails to climb trees, or simply hang their bodies upside down from tree branches by their tails. Their tails have gradually become specially adapted for this purpose: we call them "prehensile tails," which means this.

Some animals, because they live in the water a lot, their tails have a rudder-like function. It's not really the fish's, but the great whales use their formidable tails for propulsion in the water. The kangaroo's tail is also extremely developed, and it uses it to support its body weight. When it stands upright, its tail and two hind legs become a very stable tripod, and even a skilled boxer would not easily knock down an upright kangaroo.

The above are just a few examples of the functions of the tails of some animals. The tails of many other animals each have their own functions. If you want to know more details, it is best to pay attention to on-site observations at any time.

Squirrel, Kangaroo: Two animals with extremely developed tails

Scientific Little Question

Why Are Closed-Room Coal Stoves Likely to be Fatal? 232

— Zixi

Every time the north wind howls and snowflakes flutter, many middle- and lower-class families who do not have radiators or electric stoves install coal stoves for heating, but installing coal stoves for heating is really not a good idea. Over the years, there have been many reports of people losing their lives due to coal poisoning from heating stoves. Why do people get poisoned? What exactly is the "poison"? Little friends with some scientific minds must want to ask these questions right away, right? Yes, let me tell you:

The main component of coal, coal balls, and charcoal is carbon. Once carbon is burned, it becomes a gas called carbon dioxide. If there is insufficient oxygen in the air, it cannot become carbon dioxide, but becomes carbon monoxide. Although these two terms are only different by two and one when written, carbon dioxide is not dangerous at all, while carbon monoxide can be fatal. Because carbon dioxide has absolutely no effect when inhaled into the lungs, carbon monoxide immediately combines with blood cells after being inhaled, which will make the whole body immediately feel a lack of blood cells and unable to live. Just imagine a closed-room coal stove, waiting for all the limited oxygen in the room to help the coal balls in the stove burn completely. How can carbon monoxide not be produced in the room? How dangerous! I hope everyone pays more attention.

Memory Game

Preparation: About thirty kinds of miscellaneous items, such as pencils, ink, knives, bamboo rulers, watches, envelopes, etc. Experiment: First, number each item and display them in a small room with sufficient light. At this time, the participants are all outside, and are not allowed to peek. Then, record the numbers on prepared paper and distribute them to the participants. With the items pre-arranged properly, have the participants enter in groups (three or four people per group) to carefully view the items for four minutes, then exit and record the items displayed in the room on paper as quickly as possible. The latest time allowed is no more than ten minutes.

Note: This game is simple and easy to implement. I have tried it several times when I was a Boy Scout in elementary school. As a result, the best performers could memorize more than twenty kinds of items. Because the items are mixed and listed in a small room with dazzling light, the nerves of the participants are most easily disturbed by it. (Huaiqing)

Seeking: Five issues of the Shenbao Children's Supplement from January 12th, January 19th, February 2nd, February 9th, and February 16th of this year are requested. If anyone is willing to part with them, please send them to me immediately. I am willing to exchange them for a set of children's humorous story paintings (twelve episodes).

Zai Zechang, Dormitory 64, Shanghai Guanghua Affiliated Middle School.

The Tale of a Loyal Dog (9) 233

— Xinqing

Over there was the ancient, great temple, hidden away and isolated from the modern, busy, and lively world, with white clouds floating above it all day long, countless crows circling and flying there, the sound of the wind whistling there, and at their feet lay the city of Rome.

Little Nanluo often ran into those great stones, and in a flash, he disappeared behind that dark archway. Bodehi guarded the streets outside, always wondering what magic there was inside that would attract his inseparable friend.

He had tried to run in himself a couple of times to see what was going on, dragging the milk cart up the stone steps, but was always shooed away by a big man in black with silver trim. Afraid that his little master would suffer some disaster, he patiently waited outside until the child came out, then he felt relieved.

Bodehi's unease was not because Xiao Nanluo had gone to this place: he also knew that people had to go to church; the whole village went to the dilapidated little church opposite the red windmill. What made him uneasy was that Xiao Nanluo's expression often changed every time he came out, sometimes his face was flushed, sometimes it turned pale; when he returned home, he sat quietly, not even wanting to play. He was dreaming about something, staring straight at the twilight sky beyond the waterline of the canal, extraordinarily quiet, simply containing melancholy.

Bodehi wondered what it was for. He thought that it was unnatural and should not be for a small child to suddenly become so serious. So he tried his best to get Xiao Nanluo to play with him in the sunny fields, or stroll around the busy market.

But Xiao Nanluo did not go to the small church: he often went to the largest temple; Bodehi waited on the stone steps outside the iron gate, sliding his body and lying on the ground, yawning and sighing, and constantly calling, but to no avail, until the child came out of the iron gate, put his arms around his neck, kissed his yellow broad forehead, and always murmured the same two sentences: "I just want to see them, Bodehi! - I just want to see them!"

Short Story The Snowman Comes to Life 234

— Made by Mi Wenhuan

Special Telegraph Edition

Contraction and Development 235

— Zhen

The telecommunications business, which is run by the Ministry of Communications, has made remarkable achievements in terms of engineering construction, business improvement, and personnel reorganization, whether in telegraph or telephone. This publication has repeatedly published concise texts and figures based on facts, which are well known to the public. However, telecommunications construction requires a lot of money, such as the purchase of pole lines, the transportation of parts, and the installation of projects, which cannot be done without huge construction costs. The consumption of materials by the National Telegraph and Telephone Bureaus, the salaries of employees, and the expenditure of public funds also require huge maintenance costs. At this time of economic hardship in telecommunications, and without the provision of national treasury subsidies every year, it is quite difficult to maintain the status quo, and it is really difficult to talk about development! The transportation authorities have encountered this difficulty and are thinking about ways to overcome it.

Generally speaking, those who talk about financial management are nothing more than increasing revenue and reducing expenditure. The former is different for state-owned enterprises and private enterprises, and the telecommunications business is different from other state-owned enterprises. There are two ways to increase revenue in telecommunications: on the one hand, the equipment in telecommunications engineering should be improved to the utmost, so that communication efficiency can be increased; on the other hand, the handling of telecommunications business should be extremely simple, so that the public feels satisfied and is happy to use it, then the business will develop and income will naturally increase. These two are the policies currently held by the Ministry of Communications, and have been proven to be quite successful. There are also two ways to reduce expenditure: Reducing construction costs and saving maintenance costs. Compared with European and American countries, China's telecommunications business has lagged behind. If we do not actively build it, how can we form the conditions of a modern country? Therefore, construction costs must increase every year, and there is really no possibility of reducing them. As for saving maintenance costs, it can be implemented as much as possible under the principle of not hindering engineering construction and business development. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications' method of reducing expenditure focuses on saving maintenance costs, which is in line with the principle of industrial rationalization.

Recently, it was reported in the newspaper that "Due to the deficit in telecommunications, the Ministry of Communications should strive to contract. From February 25th, all maintenance material costs for various telegraph bureaus and radio stations, as well as miscellaneous transportation expenses for line maintenance workers, will be reduced by 10% according to the estimated amount. The maintenance material costs for various telephone switchboards and lines will be reduced by 20%, saving a total of more than one million yuan." This sum of more than one million yuan would be a normal expenditure in times of economic abundance, and there would be no criticism. If it can be contracted by one cent in times of economic difficulty, it will have a one-cent effect. During the national crisis, it should be even more necessary to implement contraction and work hard. We deeply admire the hard work of the transportation authorities.

"Contraction" and "development" seem to be contradictory but actually complementary terms. "Contraction" should be within the scope of not hindering the "development" of the business, and seeking "contraction" in "development" will enable the business to move forward. "Development" should use "contraction" as a means, and seeking "development" in "contraction" will enable the business to be maintained. The "contraction" policy recently implemented by the Ministry of Communications implies the use of the "development" policy, and the "development" policy to be implemented in the future will receive the results of the "contraction" policy. That is, "contraction" is "development," and "development" is "contraction." Only by understanding the principles in this can we talk about the economic policies implemented by modern countries.

Requesting the Military Authorities to Find Ways to Stop the Tapping of Military Telephones on Telegraph Lines 236

— Hua

For the sake of maintaining local security and suppressing the remaining bandits, the local garrison often taps military telephones on telegraph lines to communicate news. The reporter believes that tapping military telephones on telegraph lines not only hinders communication of news, but also inevitably makes military communications difficult. Therefore, he wrote in detail about its advantages and disadvantages in the 46th issue of this publication, and extended his hopes for the understanding of the military authorities. However, in recent months, the tapping of military telephones on telegraph lines has been heard from time to time. Although the transportation authorities have communicated with them in writing, there has been little effect. The reporter deeply knows that the act of tapping military telephones has a great impact on telecommunications and the general public, and he urgently hopes to fulfill his civic duty, express his views, and appeal to our military authorities again.

According to recent years, in order to promote telephone traffic, the Ministry of Communications has specially opened long-distance telephones on telegraph branch lines in various regions as much as possible to facilitate communication. Therefore, the circuits are used for both telegraphs and telephones, and the load is already very heavy in peacetime. If it is occupied by the military, not only will the load increase and communication be blocked, but also because the branch lines are all single-line connections, there will inevitably be excessive leakage, and it will be impossible to make calls. Therefore, occupying money for communication is a harmful and unhelpful act when it is not a last resort. Even if you want to make a call, you must consult with the local telegraph bureau to find a proper way to connect and open the money, so as to avoid all difficulties. This should be noted by the military authorities.

In addition to being open to the public, inland long-distance telephones must also be used for highway traffic communication. Therefore, the smooth flow of telephone calls is of great importance to the safety of traffic. Recently, long-distance telephones along the Xi'an (from Chang'an, Shaanxi to Lanzhou, Gansu) highway were occupied by the military, resulting in serious danger. We understand the military authorities' painstaking efforts to maintain security, but we must also take into account the current facts and make thorough contacts with the relevant parties, so that both parties can benefit! This should be noted by the military authorities.

Although, as far as we know, the military authorities have also repeatedly ordered the prohibition of tapping military telephones on telegraph lines. However, in order to save trouble, the local garrison often acts expediently. We hope that the military authorities will thoroughly inform the relevant troops, or issue temporary telephone regulations for marching, and implement them earnestly, so as to seek the flexibility of military communications without hindering the principle of public communication. This is also what we would like to ask the military authorities to pay attention to.

In short, what we ask the military authorities to cooperate with are the following points: Please do not tap military telephones unless it is a last resort. If you want to tap military telephones, please control the communication troops and implement them earnestly. If the above three points can be implemented, we believe that it will benefit both telecommunications and military communications.

The Main Uses of Telegraph in Commerce 237

— Tao Gong

In modern times, commerce has progressed, and the techniques of competition have also progressed. Commercial competition is the same as military competition, and both require weapons, so it is called "commercial warfare," but the methods and nature are different. There are different weapons in commercial warfare, and the telegraph is one of them. The concept that "military affairs require speed" also applies to commercial warfare. Therefore, the telegraph occupies an important position in commerce because of its unique speed. Up to now, all intelligent and insightful businessmen use the telegraph to flexibly handle all matters of commercial exchange, because this is the only way to achieve the effect of "responding to the opportunity quickly." Although it requires some telegraph fees, the benefits gained far exceed hundreds or thousands of times! However, there are still many people in the business world who do not know how to use this powerful weapon to compete with others. Most of these people do not understand the importance and use of the telegraph in commerce, so they cannot profit as much as those who make good use of the telegraph. It is really a pity! We who serve in the telecommunications industry have always treated business people equally, regardless of rank. We hope that everyone can enjoy the benefits of the telegraph, and we do not want it to be exclusively enjoyed by a part of the people or a certain class. Therefore, we have specially written out the main uses of the telegraph in commerce and made them public so that people can have "equal opportunity"!

Ordering: If a business knows that there is a need for a certain type of goods locally, and this type of goods is extremely scarce in the market and needs to be purchased from other places, the most appropriate and rapid method is to use the telegraph. This method can avoid the rise in prices and prevent the loss of the opportunity to sell. I can give a simple example to prove the effectiveness of telegraph ordering: I remember in the summer of the year before last, the weather in Nanjing was very hot, and the Jinpu Railway Office transported a batch of Texas watermelons, which were large and sweet, and they were immediately sold out in the market. A local fruit merchant saw that these Texas melons were popular and believed that there was a profit to be made, so he sent a telegram to the Texas melon merchants to order a large batch, and began to pre-sell them. Before the goods arrived, they had already been disposed of, and the profits tripled. At the same time, several other fruit merchants also ordered goods from Texas, but unfortunately they used mail. By the time the letters had been exchanged and the negotiations had been completed, and the goods had arrived in Beijing, the hot weather had subsided, and the selling price had plummeted. This business almost lost money. The stores that did not use telegraph ordering could only sigh at their bad luck!

Contraction Policy 238

Demanding Payment: The use of telegraphs to demand payment is not yet popular in our country, but it has been practiced for many years in European and American countries and is very common. Now demand telegraphs occupy an important position in telegraph operations in European and American countries, which shows that they are generally effective. Originally, there are indeed advantages to using telegraphs to demand payment. The first is speed, which can avoid the drawbacks of delaying days in letter exchanges and obtain the benefit of collecting the principal and interest of the payment early. The second is reliability. In our country, people generally have the psychology that "telegrams are urgent." If telegraphs are used to demand payment, it will of course easily attract the attention of the payer and have them pay off the bill as soon as possible. If there is unstable news about the customer, using telegraphs to demand payment is indeed fast and effective.

Reporting Accounts: Some people in our country have already used telegraphs to report accounts, but not very many. In European and American countries, it has been popular for a while. Large businesses with many branches mostly use this system to control the finances of branches in various places. Therefore, it is very convenient for the head office to investigate the daily accounts of branches in various places. In this way, the problem of branches obscuring accounts will naturally not occur. In recent years, there have been many emerging large businesses and factories in various parts of our country. For the sake of business safety, it is really necessary to use telegraphs to report accounts.

Reporting Market Prices: Market price fluctuations are related to business gains and losses. If you use letters to report, it will take days and the losses will be worrying. If you use telegraphs to report, then you will know immediately when it goes up or down! What kind of goods should be entered or sold, and what kind of goods should be purchased more or less, can be done with the market price telegram as a compass. Earning profits in business can be held in your hand.

In addition, such as being unable to turn around and asking others for help; remittance checks being stopped for some reason; a lack of finished goods and notifying them to rush production; and sudden changes in the market and reporting news, etc., can all use the telegraph to transmit and obtain satisfactory results. In short, the uses of the telegraph in commerce are extremely wide and broad. Due to the limited space in this publication, we cannot list them all one by one. The key lies in the businessman's ability to use it well.

News Telegraphs and News Telephones 239

— Lin

According to Article 68 of the International Telegraph Convention, all telegrams whose texts are exclusively devoted to news such as political business news, for publishing in newspapers and other periodicals, are permitted to be charged at a reduced rate as news telegrams. Based on this principle, the Ministry of Communications specially reduces the price of news telegrams to one-quarter of the ordinary telegram price, and has formulated a type of news telegram regulations, which stipulates in detail the methods for sending news telegrams.

The reason why news telegrams are given special treatment is that newspapers, in addition to being businesses, also contain a kind of social education meaning. Their role is not only for the transmission of news and the release of political information. For example, the promotion of national culture and the instilling of people's knowledge are greatly dependent on newspapers for their promotion. The level of cultural standards of a country and the popularity of social education can be estimated from the number of newspapers and other periodicals. However, in addition to the local news, most of the pages of newspapers are news materials provided by various domestic and foreign sources. This material, known as news, must be the latest news. If it discloses materials that have lost their timeliness, it is inevitable that there will be a "yesterday's flower" reproach. In order to seek the latest news, its transmission must be mainly swift, so the news from various places mostly relies on telegram transmission, which is the so-called news telegram. If news telegrams must also be charged at the same rate as ordinary telegrams, then this telegram fee will inevitably be very large. General newspaper companies have limited capital and will naturally find it difficult to bear, which will directly affect the business of newspapers and indirectly hinder the development of cultural undertakings. Therefore, all countries unanimously recognize that news telegrams should be charged at a reduced price compared to ordinary telegrams.

Some say: "Telegrams and telephones are both powerful tools for communication. Since news telegrams can be given preferential treatment and reduced prices, why can't we follow this precedent and stipulate a news telephone price reduction method? And why does the International Telegraph Convention only have regulations on news telegrams and not on news telephones? What is the reason?" This statement is not unreasonable from one aspect, but from another aspect, if we analyze the fundamental differences between telegrams and telephones, it is not difficult to understand why news telephones are uniquely lacking. According to the significant difference between telegrams and telephones, the content transmitted by telegrams is expressed in words, while telephones rely solely on dialogue. How is the content of what the two parties are talking about? Third parties have no way of finding out. Moreover, since news telegrams are only charged one-quarter of the ordinary telegram price, the content of their transmission should be absolutely limited to news. Therefore, Article 16 of the News Telegram Regulations stipulates: "The text of news telegrams is limited to news about politics and commerce that is to be published in newspapers or periodicals, and must not contain words of a private nature or similar to advertisements." Article 69 of the International Telegraph Regulations also stipulates: "News telegrams must not contain sentences of a private nature." The sincerity is that news telegrams are charged at a specially low rate. If it is not regulated, it is inevitable that someone will use the name of news telegrams to transmit telegrams that do not conform to the nature of news in order to gain cleverness. It is very obvious whether the content of telegrams, which are expressed in words, is consistent with news telegrams. As for telephones, it is difficult to verify whether the questions and answers between each other conform to news telephones. For this reason, there are no precedents for specially reducing the price of news telephones in various countries. Whether it is a city telephone installed by news reporters, newspapers, or magazine companies, or a long-distance telephone sent, the fees are charged according to regulations. However, in terms of long-distance telephones, the United Kingdom, the United States, and other countries have night-time call price reduction methods to ease the volume of calls. Although this method applies to the entire public, it is especially beneficial to news undertakings because news telephone calls are mostly made at night.

The Ministry of Communications of our country also formulated the night-time call price reduction method for long-distance telephones last year, stipulating that the night-time prices of all ordinary and expedited calls should be calculated at 70% of the daytime prices. From December 1st of last year, it was first tried out in seven places: Nanjing, Shanghai, Hangzhou, Zhenjiang, Wujin, Wuxi, and Wuxian for three months. After its implementation, all sectors of the news media deeply felt the convenience. Now that the trial period has expired at the end of February, it is heard that the Ministry of Communications believes that the results of the past three months of trial operation have been very good, and intends to continue to hold it, which is also a kind of preferential treatment for news telephones.

Supplement to the Regulations on Paid Public Telegram Charges 240

— Zhongxian

The content and advantages of the newly revised unified regulations on paid public telegram charges have been published in this journal. It is assumed that most senders and receivers are already familiar with its application, so there is no need for further explanation. The various provisions in these regulations apply equally to all Chinese and foreign language telegrams. Therefore, Article 3 stipulates: "If the sender supplements or corrects any part of the original telegram, all supplemented or corrected words shall be charged per word." However, the above provision is considered slightly inconvenient for senders supplementing or correcting the name and address of the recipient of a Chinese telegram. For example, if a sender sends the following telegram: "Shanghai Jianghai Customs Huang Zi'an 'Funds remitted'" and the receiving office informs that the recipient is no longer at Jianghai Customs and the telegram cannot be delivered, and the sender intends to use a paid public telegram to notify the receiving office to correct the recipient's name and address to "283 Dunhou Lane, Avenue Joffre, French Concession, Huang Ziliang," a total of fourteen characters. According to the aforementioned charging regulations, a fee of one yuan and forty cents should be paid for fourteen characters. However, if the sender does not use a paid public telegram, but sends another telegram as follows: "Shanghai French Concession Avenue Joffre Dunhou Lane 283 Huang Ziliang—Funds remitted," according to the current General Regulations for Domestic Telegram Business (the receiving location name is counted as two characters, the recipient's name and address are counted as three characters, and the telegram text is counted as three characters), the entire telegram only requires a fee of eighty cents, which is cheaper than sending a paid public telegram by sixty cents. Therefore, the provisions of Article 3 of the paid public telegram charging regulations are quite inconvenient for short Chinese telegrams. Now, the Ministry of Communications has instructed that Article 3 of the current unified paid public telegram charging regulations be supplemented and revised as follows:

"If the sender supplements or corrects any part of the original telegram, all supplemented or corrected words shall be charged per word (for example, supplementing an address of two characters shall be charged for two characters, correcting one character of the telegram text shall be charged for one character). However, if the sender supplements or corrects the recipient's address of a Chinese private telegram, all supplemented or corrected words shall be charged according to the provisions of Article 83 of the General Regulations for Domestic Telegram Business. (For example, if supplementing or correcting the address of a common language telegram in Chinese does not exceed thirteen characters, it shall be charged as three characters.)"

After the implementation of the above supplementary measures, if a sender uses a paid public telegram to supplement or correct the recipient's name and address of a Chinese telegram, all supplemented or corrected words can be charged according to the provisions of Article 83 of the General Regulations for Domestic Telegram Business. That is, if the recipient's name and address, totaling no more than thirteen characters in plain language or no more than fourteen characters in code, can be charged as three or four characters respectively. If this limit is exceeded, additional charges will be added. Then, even though the above paid public telegram supplementing the recipient's name and address has as many as fourteen characters, only a fee of forty cents needs to be paid, which is still cheaper than sending another telegram. The general sender will certainly be happy to adopt it, in order to save money. From this, it can be seen that although the supplementary modification of the paid public telegram charging regulations is a small reform, it is quite beneficial to the sender.

Progress Overview of the Nine-Province Long-Distance Telephone Project 241

— Ming

The Ministry of Communications is planning to establish long-distance telephone lines in nine provinces, including Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Henan, Hebei, Shandong, Jiangxi, Hunan, and Hubei. This is the largest telecommunications project in recent years. After the entire project is completed, the major cities in the above provinces will be able to communicate with each other, which will greatly benefit public communications and is of no small significance. The construction progress may be something that the public is interested in hearing about. The progress is described as follows:

Since the scope of this long-distance telephone project is too wide and the lines are long, the names of the planned lines are determined first, and each line is planned into several sections, and then the construction is carried out in sections. Therefore, since the start of construction, the progress of pole erection and line installation has been quite rapid. The following eight lines have been completed:

Jinan to Qingdao line. The Jinan-Qingdao section already had two pairs of long-distance telephone lines open for communication. Now, after adding and reconstructing, there are three pairs of telephone lines and one pair of phantom lines. With the increase in lines, communication will naturally be more convenient.

The line installation project between Suzhou and Jiaxing was completed on February 15th.

The completed sections of the Nanjing-Tianjin long-distance telephone line include the Nanjing-Xuzhou section and the Jinan-Tianjin section.

The Nanjing-Hankou long-distance telephone line is divided into five sections. Among them, the completed sections include Nanjing-Shunan, Hukou-Yangxin, and Yangxin-Hankou. The sections still under construction are Shunan-Gujiahui Anqing, and Yinjiahui-Hukou.

The Nanjing-Hangzhou long-distance telephone line is divided into two sections. The Yixing-Wuxing section has been completed, and the Wuxing-Hangzhou section will begin construction soon. The line is short, so the completion date should not be far off.

The Hankou-Changsha long-distance telephone line is also divided into two sections. The completed section is Hankou-Yueyang, and the remaining Yueyang-Changsha section is under construction and will be completed soon.

There was already a direct telegraph line between Tongshan and Zhengxian. It has now been decided to add long-distance telephone lines to the existing poles to achieve twice the result with half the effort. The line addition project will begin soon.

The long-distance line installation project between Zhengxian and Hankou is currently being carried out in five sections and will also begin construction soon.

As for the other lines, they are either being planned and carried out, or will soon begin construction. The completion of the entire project is not far off. Many members of the public are concerned about this long-distance telephone project, so a brief report on its actual progress is presented.

Telecommunications News 242

— Reporter

Navigation Safety: Adoption of Unique Electrical Machinery

The U.S. Department of Commerce recently stipulated new regulations to enhance navigation safety and facilitate rescue operations. It ordered regular transport ships sailing on the ocean to equip their lifeboats with a radio capable of transmitting signals over a distance of at least fifty miles. In case of distress, maritime rescue agencies or other ships within a fifty-mile radius can rush to rescue without delay. This electrical machinery can still operate normally when splashed with seawater. Even if completely submerged in seawater, it will not completely lose its efficiency in a short period of time. It is reported that this regulation will be implemented from New Year's Day this year.

Creation of Wireless Wind and Rain Detection

The invention of a wireless wind detector can not only respond to the movements of future hurricanes, but also measure snowfall, blowing sand, and various climate changes. According to testers, this device can distinguish various storms and emit different influences. Using this method, accurate records can be kept of the nature, location, path, and speed of future wind and rain. After repeated testing, even very subtle snow, wind, and rain can be measured and obtained, and can reach a distance of three hundred miles.

The Significance of the Ministry of Communications' Survey of Broadcast Listeners' Opinions 243

— Yu Zhou

The most important and most difficult problem to solve in rectifying the broadcasting industry is the broadcasting program. Now, the engineering design of a broadcasting station is of great importance. However, it only needs a one-time rectification. Even if there are shortcomings, it will only cause unstable frequencies and interference, making the broadcast sound not very clear. If the broadcasting program needs constant attention, and if it is not handled properly, the effect will not be achieved and the harm will be endless.

How can a broadcasting program be considered appropriate? The purpose of running a broadcasting business should be considered first. The purpose of running a broadcasting business can be put very simply: "Promote proper entertainment and promote social education." If this statement is not flawed, then the broadcasting program should contain two elements, namely "interest" and "educational significance." These two elements each have their limits. If each broadcasting station only considers the "interest" element, they often cater to the public's psychology, lower the standard, and broadcast extremely vulgar and crude programs, which are detrimental to social morality. If only the "educational element" is considered, using the function of broadcasting to promote academics, announce government orders, and convey news, this is certainly not objectionable, but given the lack of widespread education in our country and the low desire for knowledge among the public, how many of the hundreds of thousands of radio users can sit upright and listen respectfully to this kind of program lacking "interest" after a day of tiring work? Its actual effect is actually very small. Generally speaking, most people who install radios do so for leisure and entertainment, focusing on the "interest" element, while those responsible for supervision, standing in the position of the government, often focus on the "education" element. Historically, the Ministry of Communications has repeatedly rectified broadcasting programs over the years, such as prohibiting the broadcast of lewd songs and tunes, and adding programs about party principles, civic common sense, and brief histories of national heroes. Its intentions are indeed far-reaching.

However, although broadcasting programs have been actively rectified by the Ministry of Communications, many broadcasting stations still often comply in appearance but defy in reality, and cannot effectively comply, resulting in frequent criticism from the outside. Examining the reason, most listeners take "interest" as a prerequisite. In order to attract more listeners and develop business, each broadcasting station has to make many concessions. Therefore, to effectively rectify broadcasting programs, it is necessary to adopt a more progressive method, which is to find ways to improve the level of listeners. The Ministry of Communications, in view of this, in order to examine the psychology of listeners and guide them accordingly, has developed the following survey form on broadcast listeners' opinions:

What are the criteria by which listeners evaluate broadcasting stations?

What special opinions do listeners have on broadcasting programs?

The Ministry of Communications will use the above results as a reference for rectifying broadcasting programs, and will also be able to use this to assess the performance of each broadcasting station. All radio users in Peiping and Shanghai should fill out the survey forms promptly and truthfully upon receipt, in order to facilitate the progress.

Q&A Column 245

This publication has specially opened a Q&A column. Members of the public who have questions about telegram and telephone sending and receiving procedures, or who do not understand the telecommunications regulations, or who have inquiries about telecommunications common sense, are welcome to submit their questions and we will answer them.

1. Jiangdu Liu Shiqi asks: I have secretly checked Article 112 of the General Regulations for Domestic Telegram Business, which states that the number of copies for telegram distribution should be equal to the number of recipient addresses and names. "For example, if the whole telegram has two recipient addresses and names, it should be stated "Distribute two copies," and the copy fee will also be charged for two copies." I think that the copy fee should be calculated excluding the original. For example, if the whole telegram has two recipient addresses and names, only one copy fee should be paid, because the telegraph office will naturally translate and send the original telegram to the first recipient, so there is no so-called copying, and it seems that the copy fee cannot be charged.

(Answer) When distributing telegrams for copying, except for the recipient addresses and names listed in the official military telegrams, each copy only contains one recipient address and name that should be listed in that copy. The remaining recipient names and addresses and the payment business identification "Number of copies to be distributed" or (mT) are not listed according to regulations. Each receiving office should copy and send the distributed telegram according to the number of copies indicated in the incoming telegram. The original can only be kept by the office as the basis for investigation. The copying procedures have not been reduced. Therefore, the number of copies for the copy fee of distributed telegrams should be calculated according to the number of recipient names and addresses contained in the original telegram.

2. Guiyang Wang Zicheng asks: How should the fee be charged for sending or copying a telegram in this city using a telegraph machine, and how should the fee be charged for sending a telegram from the bandit suppression army in this city? Please let me know.

(Answer) The fee for sending a telegram in this city, whether transmitted by machine or copied, is charged according to the local price. (That is, the fee is charged at one-quarter of the original price.) As for the bandit suppression army telegrams, a material fee of fifty cents per hundred words should still be charged according to regulations.

3. Nanjing Hu Jie asks: I previously installed a telephone. Now I plan to transfer it to a friend. The telephone does not need to be moved. I don't know how much the telephone bureau needs for the procedure fee?

(Answer) Users who voluntarily come to the bureau to change the name or transfer the account do not need to pay a name change fee or a transfer fee. If the bureau is not notified and it is found out, a name change fee of five yuan or a transfer fee of ten yuan should be paid. Please refer to the "Name Change and Transfer" section of Chapter 6 of the Ministry of Communications' General Regulations for City Telephone Business.
